Course 1 of 288
Course Name: Speed Typing Test Assessment
Course Description: The Speed Typing Test Assessment is designed to assess your typing speed and accuracy within a set time limit. You will be required to type a given passage as quickly and accurately as possible. The test measures your words per minute (WPM) and accuracy percentage, providing valuable insights into your typing proficiency. This assessment is ideal for individuals looking to improve their keyboarding skills, enhance workplace efficiency, or prepare for roles that require fast and accurate typing.
Course Overview: The Speed Typing Test Assessment evaluates your typing speed and accuracy under timed conditions. This assessment helps measure your proficiency in fast and error-free typing, a crucial skill for various professional and academic settings.
Duration (minutes): 5
Units:
- Unit 1: Typing Assessment
  - Start Typing Assessment

You will gain insight into the process of setting up a security service business, including understanding local laws, obtaining permits, and ensuring compliance with industry standards. Additionally, the course explores best practices for hiring, training, and managing security personnel, as well as maintaining ethical and professional standards in the field. Whether you are aspiring to start your own security company or seeking to understand the business side of the security industry, this course provides the knowledge and tools needed to succeed.
Course Overview: This course outlines the essential requirements for becoming a security service provider, including legal qualifications, certifications, and industry standards. Learn the key steps to start and operate a security business successfully.

Course 4 of 288
Course Name: Carrying Out Basic First Aid Treatment in the Workplace
Course Description: This comprehensive course introduces the core principles, legal responsibilities, and practical applications of first aid within the workplace. Learners will explore the ethical and legal framework that guides first aid practice, including the responsibilities of a first-aider and patients’ rights. Emphasis is placed on initial assessment through the primary and secondary survey techniques, as well as the application of life-saving interventions such as managing airway obstructions, controlling bleeding, and treating shock. Participants will also learn how to assess and manage injuries including fractures, dislocations, and sprains, and how to utilise and maintain a workplace first aid kit in compliance with health and safety regulations. Key areas of study include: Legal and ethical principles of first aid, Emergency scene assessment and patient prioritisation, Management of airway, breathing, and circulation emergencies, Recognition and treatment of shock and severe bleeding, Supportive care for fractures and soft tissue injuries, First aid equipment readiness and kit maintenance. By the end of this course, learners will possess the confidence and competence to administer basic first aid and manage emergency situations safely and effectively within a workplace setting.
Course Overview: Immediate, informed action during medical emergencies can significantly reduce harm and save lives. This course equips learners with the foundational knowledge and hands-on skills required to carry out basic first aid treatment in the workplace. Covering essential procedures from legal compliance to triage, emergency assessment, injury management, and the use of first aid kits, the course prepares participants to respond calmly, effectively, and responsibly in a variety of workplace medical incidents.
Duration (minutes): 90
Units:
- Unit 1: q
- Unit 2: Topic 5: Airway Obstruction and Rescue Breathing
  - 1. Airway Obstruction.
  - 2. Methods of Opening the Airway.
  - 3. Partial Airway Obstruction.
  - 4. Total Airway Obstruction.
- Unit 3: Topic 3: The Primary Survey
  - 1. Assessing and Managing Emergency Situations.
  - 2. The Call For Help.
- Unit 4: Topic 6: Shock
  - 1. Definition and Causes of Shock.
  - 2. Signs and Symptoms of Shock.
  - 3. Treatment for Shock.
- Unit 5: Topic 8:  Fractures, Joints and Pelvic Injuries
  - 1. Definition, Types, and Treatment of Fractures.  2. Sprains and Strains.
  - 3. Dislocations.
  - 4. Types and Uses of Splints.
- Unit 6: Topic 9: First Aid Kit
  - 1. First Aid Kit.
  - 2. Contents of a First Aid Kit.
  - 3. Maintaining a First Aid Kit.
- Unit 7: Topic 4: The Secondary Survey
  - 1. Patient History.
  - 2. Head to Toe Physical Examination.
- Unit 8: Topic 1: Legal Compliance
  - 1. Principles and Ethics of First Aid.
  - 2. Responsibilities and Legal Principles of a First-Aider.
  - 3. Patient Rights, Monitoring, and Handover Procedures in First Aid.

Course 6 of 288
Course Name: Apply Legal Aspects in a Security Environment
Course Description: This course provides comprehensive insights into the legal framework necessary for security professionals to operate within the boundaries of the law while ensuring public safety. You’ll explore critical topics such as Human Rights and the PSIRA Statutory Code of Conduct, both of which form the ethical backbone for security practices. Delve into Criminal Law and learn the correct procedures for effecting arrests to avoid liabilities. The course also covers specific legislative acts relevant to security, including the Liquor Act, Explosives Act, Dangerous Weapons Act, and Firearms Control Act. Practical training on issues like trespassing, searching protocols, and managing public gatherings under The Public Gathering Act is included, equipping you with the legal knowledge to handle diverse security situations confidently and responsibly.
Course Overview: Gain essential knowledge of the legal principles that guide security professionals in their daily responsibilities. This course covers the application of laws in the security environment, focusing on human rights, statutory codes, criminal law, lawful arrest, and industry-specific regulations. Learn how to handle incidents involving trespassing, dangerous substances, and public gatherings while adhering to legal standards.
Duration (minutes): 90
Units:

Ideal for food industry workers, caterers, and those in hospitality, this course promotes public health and reduces the risk of foodborne illnesses.

Course 10 of 288
Course Name: Sell Products to Customers in a Wholesale and Retail Outlet
Course Description: This course provides a step-by-step framework for delivering a successful customer-focused sales experience. Learners begin by mastering the art of first impressions—approaching customers, creating a welcoming environment, and identifying their needs through effective questioning. The course then explores how to match products to customer requirements, explain features and benefits, and recommend complementary items in line with company policy.

As the course progresses, learners develop the skills to handle questions and objections confidently, applying structured techniques to maintain customer trust and engagement. In the final unit, participants learn to recognise buying signals, close sales professionally, and deliver meaningful after-sale support, including payment options and follow-up. By the end, learners will be equipped to deliver a complete, polished sales process that enhances customer satisfaction and supports business growth.


Qualifying learners will be capable of establishing the customer's needs through detailed assessments and empathetic communication. They will be proficient in offering products tailored to meet these needs, presenting options clearly and convincingly. Additionally, they will be skilled in overcoming customer objections, using effective strategies to alleviate concerns and build confidence in the purchase. They will also excel in closing the sale, ensuring a positive and seamless experience for the customer, and setting the stage for future business opportunities.
Course Overview: Effective selling is more than a transaction—it’s about connection, confidence, and customer care. This course empowers learners to guide customers through the sales journey with professionalism and purpose, turning interest into loyalty.
Duration (minutes): 180
Units:
- Unit 1: Unit 3: Overcome customer objections
  - 1. All customer questions or comments are responded to in a manner that should satisfy the customer according to organisational procedures. 2. Techniques for overcoming customer objections to the product/service are explained according to store procedures. 3. Various types of customer objections to the product/service are identified according to store procedures. 4. Customer objections to the product/service are analysed, and appropriate techniques are used to overcome the objection according to organisational procedures and guidelines. 5. Alternative products are offered if the original product does not meet the customer's need according to organisational procedures and guidelines.
- Unit 2: Unit 4: Close the sale
  - 1. Closing or buying signals are identified using the customer's feedback. 2. Appropriate techniques for closing the sale are used according to store procedures. 3. The customer is reassured of the decision taken and thanked in a way that will encourage future support according to organisational procedures and guidelines. 4. After-sale service is explained to customers where applicable according to the organisation's policy and procedures. 5. The various forms of payment options available to the customer are explained as they apply to the outlet.
- Unit 3: Unit 2: Offer products to customers
  - 1. Customer's needs are analysed, and matched with products in relation to the available products. 2. Features and benefits of products offered are explained and demonstrated according to the products characteristics. 3. The policy for selling additional products is explained as per organisational requirements. 4. Additional products that support the original sale are identified and offered as per the customer's need.
- Unit 4: Unit 1: Establish the customer's needs
  - 1. The customer is approached in a manner that encourages continued interaction according to organisational procedures and guidelines. 2. A comfortable and inviting atmosphere is created according to organisational procedures and guidelines. 3. Questioning techniques are used to identify the customer's needs according to organisational selling techniques. 4. Confirmation of the identified need is obtained from the customer according to organisational procedures and guidelines.

Course Name: Factors That Impact on the Bottom Line of a Wholesale and Retail Unit
Course Description: This course explores the key factors that influence the financial performance of wholesale and retail operations, offering learners insight into how everyday activities connect to the bottom line. Participants will examine profit concepts, cost structures, pricing strategies, and operational impacts, from stock management to staff behaviour. By mapping individual responsibilities to broader business outcomes, the course empowers retail professionals to make informed, value-driven contributions within their roles.
Course Overview: Where margins are thin and every decision counts, understanding the quiet forces shaping profit becomes a skill as vital as the sale itself.
Duration (minutes): 210
Units:
- Unit 1: Unit 3: Explain how your own job can impact on the bottom line of a business
  - 1. Own area of responsibility is explained in terms of its impact on sales. 2. Own area of responsibility is explained in terms of its impact on expenses. 3. Own area of responsibility is explained in terms of its impact on shrinkage and losses. 4. The impact that own job has on service delivery is explained as it applies to both internal and external customers. 5. The impact that own job has on the marketing and promotional activity of the business is explained as it applies to both internal and external customers. 6. The impact that own productivity has on the bottom line is explained as it applies to the business.  7. Own area of responsibility is explained in terms of its impact on stock and cash flow.
- Unit 2: Unit 2: Explain how net profit is arrived at in an operational unit
  - 1. The difference between gross and net profit is explained in terms of the elements taken into consideration when calculating it. 2. Expenses are explained as they apply to the organisation. 3. Factors impacting on gross profit margin are explained as they apply to the organisation. 4. The gross profit of a W&R business is calculated and explained as it applies to the organisation. 5. The net profit of a W&R business is calculated and explained as it applies to the organisation.
- Unit 3: Unit 1: Explain the relationship between the bottom line of a business and the factors that will impact on it
  - 1. The meaning of the bottom line is explained in the context of a wholesale and retail sector. 2. The influence that staff's personal traits and behaviour have on a business unit is explained in terms of the impact they have on the customers and the business unit. 3. The influence of limited and vast product ranges on a business unit is explained in terms of the impact it has on the customers and the business unit. 4. The influence that low margin products, high margin products and a mix between the two have on a business unit is explained in terms of the impact it has on the customers and the business unit itself. 5. The influence that the pricing of products has on a business unit is explained in terms of the impact it has on the customers and the business unit itself. 6. A list with explanations is compiled of any other factors that might impact on the customers and the bottom line of the particular business.  7. Introduction to Learner Management Systems 8. The impact of stock on cash flow is explained in terms of its effect on the bottom line of the business.

Course Overview: In the dynamic world of automotive service, clear communication and systematic procedures are key to customer satisfaction and operational success. This course empowers learners with the knowledge and practical skills to efficiently process vehicle service or repair requests in line with organisational procedures and industry standards. From identifying customer concerns to securing approvals and managing service documentation, each module is designed to streamline service operations while maintaining high-quality customer interaction.

Units:

  - 1. A customer's service history is retrieved from the service database according to standard operating procedures.

  - 3. The service history of the vehicle is referenced to ensure that service continuity is maintained.

  - 1. Customer concerns are determined by using s open-ended probing questions.
  - 2. Customer concerns are confirmed by using closed directed questioning methods.
  - 3. Service documentation is processed according to company procedures.

  - 2. Calm, confident and positive communication is maintained with a client in the face of stressful situations.
  - 3. Concerns and requirements of a customer are referred according to company policies and procedures.
  - 4. Communication with a client and or other persons/divisions is recorded as per company policy and procedure.
- Unit 5: Unit 6: Conclude service consultancy process
  - 1. The estimated time of collection is agreed with a customer in terms of workshop loads.
  - 2. The existing condition and contents of the vehicle is assessed and noted in accordance with company procedures.
  - 3.  A job card is made out in accordance with company procedures.
  - 4.  Customer valuables are secured according to organisational policies and procedures.
- Unit 6: Units 4: Sell service and repair options to customer
  - 1. The systems and components identified in the vehicle for further servicing are described in accordance with company/manufacturers service policies.
  - 2. A customer is advised on further requirements for safe motoring.
  - 3. Quotations for servicing/repairs are compiled according to standard company procedures.
  - 4. Approval for the further service or repair is obtained and agreed with a customer according to company policy and procedure.

Course 14 of 288
Course Name: Appraise and Valuate Used Vehicles
Course Description: Upon achieving this course, the learner will be able to thoroughly verify the status of used vehicles, conducting comprehensive inspections and evaluations to determine their condition and history. They will be adept at preparing an offer for the used vehicle, considering factors such as its age, mileage, and current market value to ensure a fair and competitive proposal. Furthermore, the learner will possess strong negotiation skills, enabling them to agree on a final offer to purchase that satisfies both the buyer and the seller. They will be capable of handling all aspects of the transaction professionally, ensuring a smooth and efficient process from initial inspection to final agreement.
Course Overview: The learner is capable of establishing the status and value of a used vehicle with a view to bring such vehicle into the organisation's used vehicle trading stock and to enhance the buying/selling opportunity of another vehicle. This course makes provision for the automotive retail industry with special reference to appraising and valuating second hand vehicles in the following categories; light commercial vehicles; passenger vehicles; recreational vehicles; motor cycles; tri-cycles; quad cycles; boats, light and heavy commercial vehicles, agricultural vehicles and off road (ATR) vehicles. The purchase of used vehicles includes local and purchases from abroad.
Duration (minutes): 130
Units:
- Unit 1: Unit 3: Agree a final offer to purchase
  - 1. The final offer is presented to the vendor in accordance with company policies and procedures. 2. The documentation is completed in accordance with company policies and procedures. 3. The signatures are obtained on the documentation according to company policies and procedures.
- Unit 2: Unit 2: Prepare an offer for the used vehicle
  - 1. The recommended trade value is determined in accordance with company policy and procedures. 2. The value of any optional extras fitted to the vehicle is determined in accordance with company policy and procedure. 3. The reconditioning costs are determined according to company policies and procedures. 4. The final offer for the vehicle is calculated in accordance with company policies and procedures and financial practices.
- Unit 3: Unit 1: Verify the status of the used vehicle(s)

  - 1. The relationship between individual differences and reactions to stress is explained with examples 2. Emotional reactions to stress are identified and an indication is given of behaviour that may be associated with each reaction 4. Behavioural reactions to stress are identified with examples
- Unit 4: Unit 5: Investigate techniques to manage stress in the workplace
  - 1. The relationship between stress and healthy lifestyle is explained with examples 2. The role of attitudes, behaviour, and management style in creating an environment in which stress is managed is explained with examples 3. Measures that can help to minimise stress in the workplace are investigated for a specific organisation or business unit 4. Techniques that can help to reduce or manage prolonged individual stress are identified in terms of reasonable accommodation and referral 5. Techniques to deal with a specific event are explored and an indication is given of when it is necessary to refer an individual for assistance
- Unit 5: Unit 4: Identify stressors related to home and the greater environment
  - 1.Non-workplace related factors that may be the cause of stress are identified with examples   2. The interrelationship between different causes of stress is explained and an indication is given of how each may impact on the other

Course 34 of 288
Course Name: Maintain and Adapt Oral/signed Communication
Course Description: Learners credited with this unit standard are proficient in using a variety of strategies to maintain effective communication in diverse contexts. They demonstrate the ability to adapt their language to accommodate socio-cultural sensitivities, ensuring respectful and appropriate interactions while still conveying their own intended meaning. Leveraging their understanding of language structures and conventions, these learners can effectively shape or decode the meaning of unfamiliar vocabulary or constructions, facilitating clear and precise communication.

Moreover, they excel in organising and presenting information in a focused and coherent manner, making their communication both engaging and easy to follow. These learners are also adept at identifying and explaining how speakers or signers influence their audiences, recognising the techniques and strategies used to impact listeners or viewers. This comprehensive skill set enables them to communicate confidently and effectively, whether in familiar or unfamiliar situations, and to understand and respond to the nuances of different communication environments.
Course Overview: This unit standard will be useful to learners who need a sound foundation of spoken/signed language ability for further language growth, and for application in real life contexts. Learners talk/sign confidently in both formal and informal contexts and /sign actively for ideas and information in interactions with other people. They are aware of the ways others speak/sign to influence listeners and audiences. In conveying their ideas and information they select language and a register that is accessible to their audience and fit for their purpose.

Units:

New words/signs are explored and meaning constructed from a range of contextual clues in order to extend vocabulary 3. Meaning in speaking/signing is supported by the appropriate use of pause, intonation/NMFs, pace, stress and a variety of sentence structures
- Unit 2: Unit 1: Use a variety of speaking and listening/signing strategies to maintain communication
  - 1. Questions to obtain information and clarify meaning are appropriate to the context, and are used to maintain interaction 2. Intonation (tone)/NMFs, volume/sign size, pace and rhythm, pitch/NMFs, stress, repetition and pacing are used in a manner that supports and conveys meaning 4. Sustained interactions reflect an ability to discuss a series of events 5. The main ideas are clearly distinguished during the interactions and are supported by information appropriate to the context and topic of discussion 6. Interactions are coherent, and conclusions and opinions that are justified by evidence and arguments during the interaction are recognised, then supported or countered 7. Own speech/signing is corrected or adapted to promote clarity and understanding during the interaction
- Unit 3: Unit 5: Identify and explain how speakers/signers influence audiences
  - 1. Speaker's/signer's choice of words, language usage, symbols, pictures and tone, sign size and pace is explored and explained in terms of impact on the audience 2. Speaker's/signer's omission or inclusion of pertinent facts and opinions is recognised and explained in terms of impact on the audience 3. The impact of different techniques of spoken/signed communication is identified and evaluated in terms of influence on selected audiences and used appropriately
- Unit 4: Unit 4: Organise and present information in a focused and coherent manner
  - 1. Speech/signing is organised in a way that makes its meaning and purpose accessible to listeners/audience. 2. Style and register suit purpose and audience 3. Information appropriate to purpose, audience and context is identified, located, selected, logically structured and presented 4. Illustrative aids used to promote understanding in the communication process are appropriate to the topic, audience and context 5. Own points of view and ideas are presented coherently in prepared and unprepared talks 6. Conclusions are formulated in clear, simple language, summarising the main evidence and stating own point of view
- Unit 5: Unit 2: Adapt speech/signing to accommodate socio-cultural sensitivities without losing your own intention
  - 1. The effects of combining the spoken/signed word with visual features and body language are explained and used appropriately with reference to purpose, audience and context 2. Intonation/NMFs is/are used appropriately to support intentions in spoken/signed texts and its impact is explained 3. The impact on interaction of using appropriate or inappropriate forms of politeness in a -specific context is explained 4. Own ideas and opinions are expressed in ways that reflect respect for others and sensitivity to socio- cultural differences and ways of constructing meaning

It also explores the intersecting factors that exacerbate vulnerability and outlines the systems and strategies in place to support survivors and prevent violence. Course Name: Strategic Supply Chain Management Concepts
Course Description: This course explores the critical link between corporate strategy and supply chain management. It begins with an in-depth analysis of strategic models, environmental factors, and organisational structures that shape corporate decisions. Learners will assess the role of change management, stakeholder alignment, and resistance to strategic shifts. Emphasis is placed on the integration of supply chain strategies at functional, business, and corporate levels. Topics such as global sourcing, value chains, ethical supply chains, and structural models—including lean and cooperative strategies—are examined. The course empowers learners to develop innovative and sustainable supply chain strategies that create competitive advantage in complex global markets.
Course Overview: Strategic supply chain management plays a vital role in enhancing corporate performance by aligning supply chain activities with broader business goals. This course provides learners with the knowledge and tools to analyse, develop, and implement supply chain strategies that support corporate strategy. Emphasising global competitiveness, innovation, and organisational alignment, the course prepares learners to make informed, strategic decisions that drive value and resilience across supply networks.
Duration (minutes): 290
Units:
- Unit 1: Unit 1: Analyse the concept of strategy and the process of developing corporate strategy
  - 1. Concepts related to corporate strategy are evaluated to determine the alignment between corporate strategy and the supply chain management strategy.
  - 2. Models of the strategy process are assessed focussing in particular on the analysis choice, implementation model.
  - 3. The importance of the environment, resources and internal and external stakeholders is evaluated to determine their impact on analysing, developing and implementing corporate strategy.
  - 4. The importance of organisational structures, cultures, and power is assessed in terms of their influence on the development and implementation of corporate strategy.
  - 5. Innovative strategies to grow and expand a business are developed and proposed.
  - 6. The availability, development and allocation of resources to support corporate strategy are analysed to determine the corporate performance.
  - 7. The Corporate strategy process is reviewed in order to propose changes to improve corporate performance.
- Unit 2: Unit 3: Analyse the contribution of strategic supply chain management to corporate strategy
  - 1. Functional, business and corporate strategies are analysed to reflect their relationships with the integration of supply chain strategies with corporate and business strategies.
  - 2. Strategic supply chain management is evaluated in terms of its contribution to corporate strategy and strategic make, do or buy decisions.
  - 3. Organisational structures and processes are analysed and aligned with strategic supply chain strategies.
  - 4. Innovative supply chain strategies are proposed to meet corporate and business targets.
- Unit 3: Unit 2: Manage change processes directed towards achieving corporate strategy
  - 1. Organisational instruments are developed to engender commitment to corporate strategy across functions, and at all levels of the organisation.
  - 2. The need for alignment between the component parts of an organisation are analysed to reflect their contribution to managing change.
  - 3. Resistance to change and strategic drift are diagnosed in order to address them through change management processes.
- Unit 4: Unit 6: Distinguish and assess various models of supply chain structures and relationships
  - 1. The validity of the development of a globalised strategic supply chain model is assessed to determine best value for money and benchmarks.
  - 2. The characteristics of adversarial and cooperative strategies are compared to reflect their appropriateness in different circumstances.
  - 3. Competence-based approaches for determining supply chain structures and relationships are applied for optimal supply chain operations.
  - 4. The lean supply model is assessed as a prescription for supply relationships.
- Unit 5: Unit 5: Assess the idea of the global supply market as a source of competitive advantage
  - 1. The validity of the global supply market is assessed as a source of competitive advantage.
  - 2. The concept of lean is evaluated to determine the importance of the removal of waste from supply chains.
  - 3. The concepts of value, added value and value chain are analysed to determine effectiveness and efficiency of supply chains.
  - 4.The sources, nature and role of power are analysed to determine the influence on supply chains.
  - 5. The use of supply chains to deliver ethical and socio-economic outcomes alongside commercial goals is justified in order to determine competitive advantage.
- Unit 6: Unit 4: Evaluate concepts underlying strategic supply chain management
  - 1. The validity of the supply chain concept is assessed both in terms of the nature of supply and the chain metaphor.
  - 2. Internal and external supply chains are analysed to reflect the flows across organisational boundaries upstream and downstream.
  - 3. The nature of supply chains is distinguished in private and public sectors.
  - 4. Drivers of change in global supply chains are diagnosed in order to propose strategies to address them.

  - 1.  Reading comprehension: Evaluating your ability to understand and interpret written passages. You may be asked to answer questions based on the content, main ideas, supporting details and inferences drawn from the given text.
  - 2.  Grammar and vocabulary: Assessing your knowledge and proper usage of English grammar rules and vocabulary. You may encounter tasks that require you to identify and correct grammar errors, select appropriate word choices or complete sentences with the correct grammatical forms.
  - 3.  Listening comprehension: Testing your ability to understand spoken English. You may listen to conversations, lectures or recorded audio clips, and be asked questions to assess your comprehension of the information presented.
  - 4.  Writing skills: Evaluating your ability to express your thoughts effectively in written form. You may be given prompts or topics and asked to write essays, paragraphs, or responses that demonstrate coherence, organisation and appropriate language use.
  - 5.  Speaking skills: Assessing your ability to communicate orally in English. You may be asked to participate in conversational tasks, describe pictures or scenarios, express opinions, or answer questions, demonstrating fluency, clarity and accuracy in your spoken English.
  - 6.  Vocabulary and idiomatic expressions: Testing your knowledge of commonly used vocabulary and idiomatic expressions in English. You may encounter tasks that require you to understand and use idioms, phrasal verbs and colloquial language appropriately.

Course Description: This course provides a practical and reflective approach to understanding and managing stress. Learners will explore the nature of real and imagined stress, examine various types of stress including emotional categories, and learn techniques for regaining control. The course delves into how perception influences stress, explores healthy coping strategies, and introduces the concept of escape routes for immediate relief. Key topics include mental wellness, maintaining a work-life balance, and understanding the 4 C’s of stress: Control, Commitment, Challenge, and Connection. By the end, learners will be empowered to identify stressors early, apply coping mechanisms, and foster long-term mental and emotional health.
Course Overview: Stress affects productivity, mental clarity, and overall well-being. This course in Stress Management equips learners with practical tools and psychological insights to recognise, understand, and manage stress effectively. Through structured topics and real-life strategies, participants will develop the ability to reduce emotional strain, maintain balance, and build resilience, both at work and in personal life.
Duration (minutes): 140
Units:
- Unit 1: Unit 1: Introduction
  - 1.1. Introduction.
- Unit 2: Unit 2: Awareness of real and imagined stress
  - 2.1. Awareness of real and imagined stress.
- Unit 3: Unit 3: Controlling stress
  - 3.1. Controlling stress.
- Unit 4: Unit 4: Categories of stress
  - 4.1. Categories of stress
- Unit 5: Unit 5: Categories of emotional stress
  - 5.1. Categories of emotional stress.
- Unit 6: Unit 6: Power of perceptions
  - 6.1. Power of perceptions.
- Unit 7: Unit 7: Escape routes
  - 7.1. Escape routes.
- Unit 8: Unit 8: Managing mental wellness
  - 8.1. Managing mental wellness.
  - 8.2. Healthy work-life Balance.
  - 8.3. The 4 C's of stress.

Course 98 of 288
Course Name: Selling to Corporate Fleet Owners
Course Description: The learner is capable of identifying and making contact with potential corporate fleet owners, providing information clearly and accurately, carrying out presentations of proposals, providing fleet purchasing options, creating and pursuing sales opportunities, agreeing on future actions with the customer, and recording details for use in future sales discussions. This unit standard makes provision for the automotive retail industry with special reference to the fundamentals of selling products to corporate fleet owners in the following categories: Light commercial vehicles, passenger vehicles, recreational vehicles, Motor cycles, Tri-cycles, Quad cycles, Boats, light and heavy commercial vehicles, agricultural vehicles and Off Road (ATR) vehicles.
Course Overview: Making contact with corporate prospects includes initiating communication to establish a connection. Meeting with decision-makers of corporate prospects entails engaging with key individuals who have the authority to make business decisions. Presenting a proposal/quotation to the corporate prospect involves showcasing offerings and terms. Obtaining necessary approval to conclude the deal is the final step in securing agreement and finalising the business arrangement.
Duration (minutes): 150
Units:
- Unit 1: Unit 3: Present a proposal/quotation to the corporate prospect
  - 1. Concerns and objections are addressed in accordance with company policy and procedure
  - 2. Viable purchasing options are formulated and presented to the client in terms of covering a range of financial commitments
  - 3. A sales presentation is compiled according to company policies and procedures within the financial capabilities of the prospective client
- Unit 2: Unit 4: Obtain necessary approval to conclude the deal
  - 1. Obtain necessary approval to conclude the deal
  - 2. Proof of approval for the deal is presented in terms of obtaining approval from the prospective customer and own management
  - 3. The terms and conditions for further dealings are compiled according to company policy and procedures
  - 4. Agreement is obtained from the prospective customer to conclude the deal
- Unit 3: Unit 2: Make contact with corporate prospects
  - 1. The most viable purchasing options are established in terms of the corporate prospects' financial position and in accordance with company procedures
  - 2. Different methods of contacting corporate prospects are explained in terms of pros and cons and research done on the prospective client
  - 3. Company policies and procedures secure an appointment with the decision-makers
  - Information is recorded with reference to the requirements and/or present status of the corporate fleet
  - 4. Company policy and procedures present information on the organisation and products relevant to the corporate prospect's requirements
  - 5. The financial position of a corporate prospect is established in terms of the envisaged sale and in accordance with company policies and procedures
  - 6. Decision-makers of prospective clients are identified prior to a sales intervention with reference to who can make a purchasing decision
- Unit 4: Unit 1: Source new corporate prospects
  - 1. The objectives for a corporate interface are explained with reference to company policy and procedures
  - 2. Corporate prospects in a specific area are identified from referred and non-referred leads
  - 3. Methods to research source leads are described with reference to the identification of related corporate prospects
  - 4. A database of potential corporate prospects is compiled to inform decisions
  - 5. Source leads are listed with reference to possible corporate clients

Units:

- Unit 3: Unit 3: Monitor and evaluate previous own sales performance against own forecasts

  - 2. A deviation report of objectives not met during previous sales months is submitted according to company procedures

Course 105 of 288
Course Name: Understanding Market Mechanisms in New Ventures
Course Description: Understanding Market Mechanisms in New Ventures provides a comprehensive examination of economic systems, market structures, and economic forces shaping business environments. The course covers the characteristics of different economic systems, the influence of competition, and how supply and demand determine prices and production. It also addresses key economic concepts such as inflation, exchange rates, and international trade, with a particular focus on their relevance to new ventures in South Africa. Learners will develop the ability to analyse market conditions and apply economic reasoning to real-world business scenarios, enhancing their strategic decision-making skills.
Course Overview: This course offers a clear and practical insight into how market mechanisms operate within new ventures. Learners will explore fundamental economic principles, the role of competition, supply and demand dynamics, and the impact of macroeconomic factors, all within the context of emerging businesses. By understanding these mechanisms, participants will be better equipped to make informed decisions that support sustainable growth and competitive advantage.
Duration (minutes): 210
Units:
- Unit 1: Unit 1: Explain the free market system in terms of perfect and imperfect competitive markets
  - 1. An explanation is given of the characteristics of different economic systems.
  - 2. The role of competition in a free market system is explained with examples from state-owned/monopolies and private businesses.
  - 3. Competition is illustrated by listing varying prices of the same product/service.
  - 4. Reasons for imperfect competitiveness are described with examples thereof.
  - 5. The advantages and disadvantages of competition are explained with examples for the consumer and business.
  - 6. A description is given of the interaction of role-players in the economic system.
  - 7. The conditions for the existence of perfect and imperfect markets are explained in relation to the South African context.
- Unit 2: Unit 2: Analyse the interaction of demand and supply in price determination
  - 1. An explanation is given of the laws of demand and supply.
  - 2. An explanation is given of the relationship between the variables of demand and supply curves.
  - 3. The relationship between demand, supply, and price is discussed with reference to own products or services.
  - 4. Factors that lead to changes in the demand and supply curve are listed in their own specific context.
  - 5. Factors of production are explained in terms of the roles and contribution to the economy.
  - 6. Money is explained in terms of its role in the economy.
- Unit 3: Unit 4: Describe the development and significance of markets
  - 1. International trade as a result of uneven distribution of resources is investigated in terms of opportunities for new ventures.
  - 2. Socio-economic factors are identified that underline the importance of new ventures in South Africa.
  - 3. Growth sectors that exist in South Africa are identified and classified for possible new ventures.
- Unit 4: Unit 3: Analyse the factors that influence economic activity
  - 1. The effects of cyclical movements in a market system are evaluated in context of a new venture.
  - 2. A description is given of the concept of inflation and its impact on the new venture.
  - 3. Reasons are identified for the decline in the value of money.
  - 4. An explanation is given for the role of foreign currency and exchange rates in the general economy.
  - 5. An explanation is given of the role of the interest/BA rate, Gross Domestic Product, and Balance of Payments in the operations of the new venture.

Course 106 of 288
Course Name: Business Planning for New Ventures
Course Description: This unit standard aims to equip learners with the necessary knowledge and skills to produce business, financial and operations plans for implementing a new venture. It will also address the economic and administrative issues that prevent starting a new venture and contribute to the inability of an entrepreneur to sustain a new venture. The qualifying learner will be able to identify, gather and analyse the relevant information needed to compile a business plan. Formulate an ethical framework for the operational plans of a new venture. Establish and prioritise business, financial and operational goals and objectives for a new venture. Design and present business, financial and marketing plans based on a budget for a new venture.
Course Overview: Gathering and analysing relevant information for a business plan, formulating an ethical framework for operational plans in a new venture, establishing and prioritising business, financial, and/or operational goals and objectives, and designing and presenting comprehensive business, financial, and/or marketing plans based on a budget are integral steps in the strategic planning process for a new business venture.
Duration (minutes): 250
Units:
- Unit 1: Unit 2: Formulate an ethical framework for the operational plans of a venture
  - 1. Legislation and relevant regulations relating to the type of venture are identified for use in drawing up a code of ethics for the business
  - 2. Non-statutory regulations applicable to the sector are identified and used for use in drawing up a code of ethics for the business
  - 3.Codes of conduct that are used by similar organisations in the sector are evaluated and elements identified for inclusion in an ethical framework for the business
  - 4. Social and ethnic considerations are identified for inclusion in the ethical framework of a new venture
  - 5. Personal values are identified for modifying an ethical framework for a new venture
  - 6. An ethical framework and codes of ethics and conduct are drawn up for the new venture
- Unit 2: Unit 3: Establish and prioritise business, financial and/or operations goals and objectives for new venture
  - 1. Personal objectives are clearly articulated and aligned to the plans of own venture
  - 2. Business objectives are analysed and specific goals formulated to achieve objectives set out for own business
  - 3. A vision statement of a new venture is compiled to represent goals and objectives set for own venture
  - 4. Specific short and long term goals are formulated allowing flexibility for possible changing circumstances
  - 5. Possible contribution to community and regional growth objectives are identified and considered
  - 6. Cultural values and beliefs of prospective employees and expected consumers are incorporated into the plans of own venture
- Unit 3: Unit 4: Design and present business, financial and/or marketing plans based on a budget for a new venture
  - 1. The business of the venture is introduced and described based on research and analyses of competitors
  - 2. Structure and layout of the business plan are designed to be compatible with the nature of own venture
  - 3. Marketing and promotion of the own venture are concisely presented in the business plan
  - 4. Finance requirements for the business are stated in the business plan
  - 5. The projected income and expense items for own venture are tabulated in the business plan
  - 6. The costs, risks, and proposed infrastructure of the operations plan are presented in the business plan of own venture
  - 7. Relevant documentation is compiled to support the business plan
  - 8. Business plan information is presented in a relevant and clear format
  - 9. Procedures to present the business plan for own venture to a financier are explained
- Unit 4: Unit 1: Identify, gather and analyse the relevant information needed to compile a plan for a new venture
  - 1. The purpose and importance of a business plan is discussed in terms of its contribution to a successful business
  - 2. The different elements of a successful business plan are listed and described with examples
  - 3. Information on the resources needed and procedures to be followed to achieve the plan is compiled
  - 4. The industry-specific and legal requirements for own venture are identified and explained in terms of how they will affect the venture

  - 3. Trends and developments in relation to product or service are monitored and product or service life cycle is determined accordingly
  - 4. Plans are made to ensure that business venture is aligned to product or service life cycle
- Unit 4: Unit  4: Incorporate market research into a marketing plan
  - 1. The elements of a marketing plan are outlined and described according to their own business context
  - 2. New venture opportunity is analysed and a marketing plan compiled in accordance with the four P's of marketing
  - 3. Measurement tools to evaluate success of marketing plans are identified and included in the plan
  - 4. Action goals are outlined and implemented, with time frames
  - 5. Reasons and methods for evaluating and modifying marketing plans are explained and implemented in the context of market research results
  - 6. Marketing plans integrated into business
- Unit 5: Unit 2: Conduct market research
  - 1. The importance of market research is explained in relation to proposed new venture
  - 2. Market research techniques are identified and explained in context of proposed new venture
  - 3. Market research tools are identified and utilised to determine viability of new venture
  - 4. Market research is conducted and factual information is gathered and interpreted in relation to own business
  - 5. Viability of new venture is determined according to market research findings

  - 5. Resources to ensure successful implementation of plan are identified and utilised on an ongoing basis
- Unit 5: Unit 3: Identify the characteristics of a typical entrepreneur

Course 112 of 288
Course Name: Stock Replenishment in a Retail Business
Course Description: This course offers a practical guide to the end-to-end process of stock replenishment in a retail environment. From determining stock needs through stock takes, to sourcing and comparing suppliers, learners will gain insight into selecting the best stock provider based on price, reliability, and location. The course also covers the transportation and receiving of goods, including secure loading methods, damage checks, and stock recording practices. Learners will explore how to identify and resolve stock discrepancies while minimising shrinkage and loss throughout the process. By the end of the course, participants will be able to confidently manage stock replenishment in alignment with organisational procedures and retail industry standards.
Course Overview: Efficient stock replenishment is vital for maintaining smooth retail operations and meeting customer demand. This course provides learners with the practical knowledge and skills to manage stock requirements, select reliable suppliers, and ensure effective transport and receiving processes. Through each stage of the stock flow, learners will develop strategies to optimise value, reduce loss, and maintain accuracy within retail inventory systems.
Duration (minutes): 180
Units:
- Unit 1: Unit 2: Transport stock
  - 1. Items for transport are collected according to stock requirements.
  - 2. The condition of the items is checked prior to leaving the provider's premises and any damaged stock is reported and/or replaced.
  - 3. Stock is loaded in an appropriate sequence and packing material and methods are used to secure and protect stock from damage/spoilage whilst in transit.
  - 4. Ways in which shrinkage and losses occur are explained in relation to the process of loading and unloading stock.
- Unit 2: Unit 3: Receive stock into the outlet
  - 1. Offloaded stock is sorted according to stock characteristics.
  - 2. The stock received is recorded according to organisational requirements.
  - 3. The stock received is checked against stock purchased.
  - 4. All variances between actual stock received and purchased are identified and resolved according to organisational requirements and procedures.
- Unit 3: Unit 1: Buy stock
  - 1. Stock requirements are determined according to stocktakes.
  - 2. The availability of stock from various sources is investigated to ensure the best price, reliability of supply and quick response time to order being placed.
  - 3. Prices of required stock available from providers are compared to ensure the best price and value for money.
  - 4. Location of providers in terms of travel costs is determined to ensure the best price and value for money
  - 5. A decision is made on which provider to use based on the above factors

Course 114 of 288
Course Name: Standard Insurance Cover in Terms of SASRIA
Course Description: This unit standard will be useful for learners in short-term insurance, intermediaries, insurers, reinsurers, underwriters and underwriting agents, claims assessors, attorneys and learners in the Ministry of Finance who give advice, arrange insurance, analyse risk exposure and settle claims. It deals with optional insurance cover that can be added to short-term insurance policies to cover riots, labour disturbances, lockouts, public disorder and acts of terrorism or violence. The qualifying learner is capable of explaining the origin of SASRIA insurance. Analysing the cover provided by SASRIA against the general exceptions in short-term insurance policies. Identifying SASRIA's territorial limits. Describing the terms and conditions of the SASRIA coupons/policies. Applying SASRIA rates to short-term insurance policies.
Course Overview: Analysing the cover provided by SASRIA involves assessing its protection against general exceptions in short-term insurance policies. Identifying SASRIA's territorial limits, describing the terms and conditions of SASRIA coupons/policies, and applying SASRIA rates to short-term insurance policies are essential steps in understanding and effectively utilising SASRIA insurance in the context of risk management.
Duration (minutes): 200
Units:
- Unit 1: Unit 3: Identify SASRIA territorial limits
  - 1. The area covered by SASRIA as described in the Reinsurance of Material Damage and Losses Act 56 of 1989, as amended, is identified on a map of Southern Africa
  - 2. The territorial limits on SASRIA in the SADC and other countries is explained and an indication is given of how SASRIA is applied in Namibia
  - 3. The application of territorial limits is explained in terms of reciprocal arrangements
- Unit 2: Unit 1: Explain the origin of SASRIA insurance
  - 1. The historical basis for SASRIA is explained with reference to the 1976 Soweto riots and the role of insurance and government at the time
  - 2. The changes to SASRIA cover since 1979 are explained with reference standing charges or working expenses and non-political riots
  - 3. The effect of legislation on SASRIA is explained with reference to the formation of SASRIA Ltd.
  - 4. An international application of the SASRIA model of insurance is researched and an indication is given of the establishment of terrorism insurance in another country
- Unit 3: Unit 4: Describe the terms and conditions of the SASRIA coupons and policies
  - 1. The loss limit on any one insured entity is explained with examples
  - 2. The relationship between the SASRIA loss limit and the Companies Act, 1973, as amended, is explained graphically for three case studies
  - 3. The SASRIA construction site loss limit is explained with examples
  - 4. The effect of the Marine Institute Clauses on premium in transportation insurance is analysed for three examples
  - 5. Reasons why cover that includes Marine Institute Clauses is charged at a lower rate for SASRIA cover are explained with reference to a claim
  - 6. The relationship between a material damage policy, SASRIA coupon and SASRIA consequential loss policy is explained graphically
- Unit 4: Unit 5: Apply SASRIA rates to short term insurance policies
  - 1. The SASRIA rating table is used to determine the rate on a personal lines policy for two examples
  - 2. The SASRIA rating table is used to determine the rate on a motor insurance policy for two examples
  - 3. The SASRIA rating table is used to determine the rate on a commercial and industrial insurance policy for two examples
  - 4. The SASRIA rating table is used to determine the rate on a transportation insurance policy for two examples
  - 5. The application of discounts on SASRIA premiums is explained with examples
  - 6. Annual adjustments to the premium that are required are explained with examples
- Unit 5: Unit 2: Analyse the cover provided by SASRIA against the general exceptions in short term insurance policies
  - 1. The standard South African Insurance Association (SAIA) general exceptions in a short term policy are analysed in terms of excluded events
  - 2. The concept of malicious damage to property in terms of SASRIA is compared to conventional non-SASRIA malicious damage to property
  - 3. Five different SASRIA coupons/policies are analysed to ascertain the cover and exclusions
  - 4. The difference between a SASRIA Ltd. coupon and a SASRIA Ltd. policy is explained with reference to terms and conditions

Course Name: Negotiation Skills in Business
Course Description: This unit standard is intended as part of a qualification for managers of small businesses and junior managers of business units in larger organisations. The term business unit in this unit standard implies a small business, cost centre, section or department. The unit standard could be useful for any employee involved in situations where negotiation skills are required. Junior managers include, but are not limited to, team leaders, supervisors, first-line managers and section heads. The positioner term describes the first level of management in an organisation at which an employee has other employees reporting to him/her. The qualifying learner can explain the need for business negotiation skills. Explaining the steps in the negotiation process. Applying the steps in the negotiation process to an authentic situation. Explaining strategies that could be used in negotiation.
Course Overview: Detailing the necessity of negotiation skills in business, outlining the steps involved in the negotiation process, applying these steps to a real-world situation, and elucidating on strategies applicable to negotiations are key components in understanding and effectively utilising negotiation skills for successful business interactions.
Duration (minutes): 250
Units:
- Unit 1: Unit 1: Explain the need for negotiation skills in business
  - 1. Reasons why managers need negotiation skills are indicated with reference to the changing nature of the workplace and democratisation
  - 2. The kind of decisions that lower level managers are required to negotiate is identified with reference to the management structure of organisation and labour legislation
- Unit 2: Unit 4: Explain strategies that could be used in negotiation
  - 1. Tactics that can be used to delay a negotiation are described with examples
  - 2. Methods that can be used to break a deadlock are explained with examples
  - 3. Different types of closure are identified and an indication is given of when each is suitable
- Unit 3: Unit 3: Apply the steps in the negotiation process to an authentic work situation
  - 1. The concepts of “favoured outcome”, “settlement point” and “point beyond which you cannot go” are explained for a selected scenario
  - 2. The disadvantages to each party for each position are considered prior to meeting
  - 3. Possible points that the other party might raise are anticipated and a possible response to each identified point is considered for the selected scenario
  - 4. A proposal is presented and a clear indication is given of what is and what is not on the table for a selected scenario
  - 5. A point-by-point summary of the proposal is compiled to ensure that both parties have a common understanding of the nature and extent of the proposal
  - 6. Questions are asked to build common ground and establish the existence of any hidden agendas
  - 7. Shared interests, opportunities for cooperation and common principles are identified in order to facilitate negotiation
  - 8. A position is amended without sacrificing fundamental interests for a selected scenario
  - 9. Questions are asked for clarification and explanation
  - 10. Questions are asked to test understanding and to summarise understanding of a position
  - 11. Demands of the other party are analysed and a concession is proposed for a selected scenario
  - 12. The negotiation is closed for a selected scenario
- Unit 4: Unit 2: Explain the steps in the negotiation process
  - 1. The steps used in negotiation are named and explained in terms of what is entailed at each step
  - 2. Reasons why negotiations fail are listed and an indication of what negotiators can do to facilitate mutually satisfactory solutions
  - 3. The abilities needed by skilled negotiators are identified and an indication is given of how each ability can contribute to the success or failure of a negotiation and at what stage of the negotiation each skill may be required

Course 130 of 288
Course Name: Finance a New Venture
Course Description: This course guides aspiring entrepreneurs through the financial planning, sourcing, and structuring necessary to fund a new business venture. From calculating capital requirements and assessing viability to comparing funding options and preparing finance applications, learners will develop the financial literacy essential for sustainable enterprise. The course also addresses personal financial readiness, collateral considerations, and compliance, ensuring informed and practical decision-making for launch and growth.
Course Overview: Before a venture breathes, its future is negotiated in numbers, this course traces the logic and strategy behind that first financial heartbeat.
Duration (minutes): 200
Units:
- Unit 1: Unit 1: Explain financial controls for managing a business
  - 1.  Funding requirements and capital structure are identified and analysed for the new venture
  - 2. Realistic fixed asset requirements are determined for the new venture
  - 3. Pre-operating costs are identified and calculated to an exact value
  - 4. Monthly operating costs - including a cash flow statement - are compiled for the new venture
  - 5. The financial viability of the proposed new venture is assessed, and the break-even point is estimated
- Unit 2: Unit 2: Identify and apply accounting practices and procedures
  - 1. An extensive list of financial institutions offering funding for new ventures is compiled to select the one best suited to the venture
  - 2. The various funding packages (products) appropriate for a new venture are investigated and compared regarding their own venture needs
  - 3. The cost of the various funding options is compared to determine suitability for one's venture's business structure
  - 4. Short-term and long-term advantages and disadvantages of the various funding options are considered and discussed in the context of one's own business and a decision is made as to the most suitable
- Unit 3: Unit 4: Utilise financial statements to identify business progress
  - 1. Collateral requirements for accessing funding are identified to determine if they can be met
  - 2. The new venture proposals are assessed in terms of available collateral
  - 3. The information and back-up documentation needed to process application for funding is collected and used to complete the application
  - 4. A financing option is chosen that is consistent with the business plan in terms of profit objectives and return on capital
  - 5. Laws, regulations, rules and procedures covering the provision and use of financial services are observed to ensure compliance
- Unit 4: Unit 3: Manage business accounts and maintain business record
  - 1. Personal income and expenditure statements are prepared for oneself based on their own financial situation over the past year
  - 2. The situations when an assets and liabilities statement is required are listed and an indication is given of the advantages of keeping such records
- Unit 5: Unit 5: Identify alternative sources to secure finance for a new venture
  - 1. The difference between debt (loans) and equity (owner's capital) is explained with reference to the new venture
  - 2. Problems faced in obtaining finance for the new venture are identified with a view to overcoming them
  - 3. Alternative sources of equity are investigated for the new venture
  - 4. Government and non-governmental schemes for new venture creation are investigated and analysed and an explanation given of their advantages and disadvantages for the new venture
  - 5. The option of leasing as a method of reducing start-up capital is considered for your own venture
  - 6. The repayments and interest rates of the alternative options are considered and compared to those of the financial institutions to make informed decisions

Course 132 of 288
Course Name: Tender Procedures for a New Venture
Course Description: This course is designed to guide entrepreneurs and small business owners through the tendering process, from initial prospecting to final submission. The course also covers the technical and financial preparation of tenders, including cost breakdowns, mark-ups, and joint venture considerations where capacity constraints exist. Emphasis is placed on compliance, meeting submission criteria, and engaging external expertise when necessary to strengthen a bid. By course end, participants will be equipped to submit professional, competitive tenders with confidence.
Course Overview: Tendering plays a crucial role in enabling new ventures to secure business opportunities in competitive markets. This course provides the foundational knowledge and practical skills needed to understand and participate in tender processes effectively. From identifying relevant tenders to submitting compliant documents, learners will develop a strategic approach aligned with their business goals and operational capabilities.
Duration (minutes): 170
Units:
- Unit 1: Unit 1: Procure and review a tender document
  - 1. A tender work prospecting system is identified and set up within the context of the business plan.
  - 2. The process of procuring a tender document is followed.
  - 3. Tender documents are reviewed to determine if it is viable to pursue tender in relation to business opportunities and risks.
  - 4.Where relevant, the prospect of pursuing tenders on a joint-contract basis with other small enterprises is determined in order to meet tender capacity and resource requirements.
  - 5. Where relevant, external sources and expertise are sought to assist in completing tender documents.
- Unit 2: Unit 2: Prepare and complete a tender document
  - 1. Information is extracted from bidders meetings and tender documents.
  - 2. The tender requirements are listed and the venture's ability to comply is determined.
  - 3. A work breakdown or product itemisation is performed.
  - 4. Allowable unit costs for all work activities or product items are calculated.
  - 5. Profit mark-ups are implemented to produce selling prices.
  - 6. The schedule of quantities or products or services are completed.
- Unit 3: Unit 3: Submit a tender document
  - 1. The completed tender document is checked to ensure compliance to criteria outlined in tender document.
  - 2. Information relating to tender submission is extracted from the tender documents.
  - 3. The tender is submitted within the time, manner and criteria stipulated in the tender document.

  - 4. A gap analysis is performed to determine where the organisation is and where it wants to be.
  - 5. Initial requirements are derived and documented in order to clarify solution scope.
- Unit 3: Unit 2: Determine an approach to identifying the most appropriate solution

  - 3. Viable potential solution approach is recommended to facilitate business decision making processes.
  - 4. A feasibility study report is produced to communicate and validate the recommended solution approach with stakeholders.
- Unit 4: Unit 3: Define the project and solution scope

Course Name: Manage and Communicate Requirements
Course Description: This unit standard will enable learners to manage conflicts and changes to requirements and ensure that all stakeholders and the project team remain in agreement on the solution scope. A learner credited with this unit standard will be able to ensure that changes to project work products are agreed upon by all stakeholders and documented accurately, maintain relationships between components to trace requirement changes and update relevant documentation, maintain requirements for re-use, prepare a requirements package, communicate requirements and changes to all stakeholders.
Course Overview: Ensuring unanimous agreement and accurate documentation of project changes among stakeholders, maintaining connections between components to track requirement modifications, preserving requirements for future use, compiling a comprehensive requirements package, and effectively communicating requirements and changes to all involved parties are essential tasks in this context.
Duration (minutes): 200
Units:
- Unit 1: Unit 1:  Ensure that changes to project work products are agreed by all stakeholders and documented
  - 1. Formal and informal changes to requirements are approved and documented to ensure that all stakeholder needs are met
  - 2. Conflicts and issues with requirements are highlighted and resolved to ensure that consensus is reached between all stakeholders regarding the most appropriate solution
  - 3. Changes to requirements are prioritised to allow the selection, design, and development of the most appropriate solution
  - 4. Multiple versions of requirements work products are maintained to ensure that changes can be traced by change control procedures
- Unit 2: Unit 2: Maintain relationships between components to trace requirement changes and update relevant documentation
  - 1. The relationships between the various requirements components are maintained to ensure consistency
  - 2. An impact analysis is performed when changes are requested to ensure the plan can be updated
  - 3. Impact analysis information is produced to ensure that agreed-upon changes are included in the process
  - 4. Support activities ensure that the solution assessment and validation include the changed requirements
- Unit 3: Unit 5: Communicate requirements and changes to all stakeholders
  - 1. The requirements package and business communication plan are used to communicate with all stakeholders appropriately
  - 2. Interaction with stakeholders takes place before, during, and after the project to ensure that they are informed and participate in decision-making
  - 3. Each activity in the business analysis process involves communication on different levels
  - 4. Interaction with the solution team to assure that requirements are correctly understood and implemented
  - 5. All requirements are communicated and understood by all parties involved in the project
- Unit 4: Unit 3: Maintain requirements for re-use
  - 1. The requirements to be maintained are selected after solution implementation
  - 2. Name the responsible party who will maintain the requirements (i.e., custodian, librarian)
  - 3. The responsible party is identified too
  - 4. Facilitate ongoing use of requirements for impact analysis and solution maintenance
  - 5. Facilitate re-use of requirements on related projects to encourage enterprise consistency of business models
- Unit 5: Unit 4: Prepare a requirements package
  - 1. Use the agreed requirements and business communication plan to determine the requirements package
  - 2. Determine appropriate format for requirements
  - 3. Create a requirement package

Through analysis and comparison, participants will learn how to assess multiple IT solution options and confidently recommend the most effective one for a given situation.
Course Overview: Understanding what affects how IT solutions are put into action, examining various methods commonly used in the IT field, and suggesting the best implementation approach for a particular situation are key aspects to explore in this discussion.
Duration (minutes): 150
Units:

  - 1. Different computer system types are distinguished for use in implementation purposes.
  - 2. Different implementation methods are examined to show how they are used in a computer system.
  - 3. The applicability of different Systems Development Lifecycle (SDLC) models to different situations are demonstrated using examples.
- Unit 2: Unit 1: Discuss the factors that influence the implementation options of  an IT solution
  - 1. Environmental factors affecting different implementation options are explained using examples to clarify each factor.
  - 2. System constraints affecting implementation options are discussed with examples of their effect.
  - 3. Reasons for selecting a computer system/solution are explained to reflect support for implementation options.
  - 4. Conversion factors are interpreted to show how they affect implementation options.
- Unit 3: Unit 3: Recommend implementation solutions for a specific context
  - 1. The factors affecting the implementation are analysed in order to recommend suitable solutions.
  - 2. Different options are identified and compared in terms of their suitability for a given scenario.
  - 3. A suitable solution is recommended for implementation within a specific context.

Through practical scenarios and organisational insights, participants will be well-equipped to manage supplier negotiations effectively.

This course builds essential negotiation skills tailored to supply chain environments, enabling professionals to approach supplier negotiations with clarity, confidence, and strategic intent. Learners will gain insights into planning, conducting, and reviewing negotiations to align with organisational goals and enhance overall procurement effectiveness.
Duration (minutes): 180
Units:
- Unit 1: Unit 3: Negotiate with the suppliers
  - 1. The negotiating atmosphere is set in terms of the negotiating strategy of the organisation.
  - 2. Proposals and counter-proposals are presented in a way that is clear and understandable to all parties in line with the organisation's strategy for suppliers.
  - 3. The negotiation process and follow-up points are recorded as required by the organisation.
- Unit 2: Unit 4: Review negotiation with the suppliers
  - 1. The negotiation process and results are reviewed in terms of the original objective set by the organisation.
  - 2. The negotiation process is reviewed to identify strengths and weaknesses in the negotiation process.
  - 3. The review identifies areas for development and recommendations for future improvement are made.
- Unit 3: Unit 2: Plan to negotiate with the suppliers
  - 1. The objectives of the negotiation is determined in terms of required outcomes as determined by the organisation.
  - 2. Factors that are or are not negotiable are identified in terms of the negotiation to take place.
  - 3. The strategy to be used is planned regarding the information and resources required to apply to the organisation.
  - 4. Possible strategies of the other parties are explored, along with responses that might be required from the negotiator to plan for negotiations.
  - 5. Fallback positions and options per planned negotiations are determined as the organisation requires.
- Unit 4: Unit 1: Describe processes & principles used when negotiating with suppliers

  - 2. The various circumstances for negotiations are described along with their objectives as it applies to the organisation.
  - 3. The relevant negotiation processes used in the organisation are described according to the process for negotiating with suppliers.

Course 195 of 288
Course Name: Cultural Awareness
Course Description: This course provides a comprehensive exploration of cultural dynamics within the South African workplace. It begins with an overview of the cultural groups represented in South Africa, followed by a historical review of intergroup conflict and the stereotypes that have shaped cultural perceptions. Learners will gain insight into the traditions and practices of both major and minor religions, and examine how political history has shaped modern cultural attitudes. The course delves into the complexities of fostering a unified yet diverse workforce and identifies ways to overcome cultural barriers. It further addresses the personal and organisational impact of the migrant labour system, explores fair versus unfair discrimination under the South African Constitution, and discusses various cultural “isms” and phobias in the workplace. Practical strategies are offered to enhance inclusivity, equity, and understanding through improved policies, behaviours, and awareness.
Course Overview: In today’s increasingly diverse South African workplace, understanding and appreciating cultural differences is vital to fostering inclusive, respectful, and productive environments. The Cultural Awareness course offers a foundational exploration of the diverse cultures present within the South African workforce. Through historical context, religious and political influence, and current workplace realities, learners will develop the knowledge and empathy required to promote harmony and equity across cultural boundaries. This course equips individuals to identify, address, and transform cultural challenges into opportunities for unity, cooperation, and shared success in a multicultural professional setting.
Duration (minutes): 190
Units:
- Unit 1: Unit 1: Analyse aspects of cultural diversity in the South African workplace
  - 1.  A listing is made of the cultures that make up the South African workplace.
  - 2. A historical overview is provided of conflicts that have existed between various cultural groups in South Africa.
  - 3. Examples are given of stereotyping and perceptions that have developed with respect to culture.
- Unit 2: Unit 2: Discuss important generic aspects of cultural groups
  - 1.  A summary is given of the cultural activities and practices associated with South Africa’s mainstream religions.
  - 2. The cultural views of at least three minor religions in South Africa are given.
  - 3. The effect that politics has played in shaping cultural attitudes in South Africa is explained using historical and present-day examples.
  - 4. The challenges inherent in creating a united, yet, culturally diverse workforce are explained with the use of examples of how the challenges may be overcome.
- Unit 3: Unit 3: Understand the needs and sensitivities of people of different cultural backgrounds
  - 1. The needs and sensitivities of people of different cultural backgrounds are identified with a view to understanding how best to meet their expectations.
  - 2. The problems associated with the migrant labour system are explained in terms of the labourer’s personal development, feeling of self-worth and family ties and responsibilities.
  - 3. Suggestions are offered for changes to policies, procedures, habits and attitudes in order to promote harmony in a culturally diverse workplace.
  - 4. A distinction is made between fair and unfair discrimination pertaining to cultural difference as provided for in the South African constitution.
  - 5. A range of “isms” and “phobias” relating to cultural difference is described in the context of the workplace.
- Unit 4: Author: SpecCon
  - SpecCon Holdings (Pty) Ltd
