This course provides learners with practical skills and knowledge to function effectively as a member of a project team. By exploring collaboration, communication, conflict resolution, and stakeholder engagement, learners will develop the competencies required to contribute positively to project outcomes and maintain a productive team environment.
Duration (minutes): 230
Units:
- Unit 1: Unit 1: Demonstrate an understanding of working as a member of a team
  - 1. Criteria and behaviours conducive to working as a member of a team are identified and explained with practical examples.
  - 2. Team interfaces are described and the roles are explained with actual examples.
  - 3. Disruptive behaviours to team performance are identified and explained with examples of the consequences.
- Unit 2: Unit 4: Respect personal, ethical, religious and cultural differences to enhance interaction between team members
  - 1. The differences between team members are identified and explained with examples.
  - 2. The importance of showing respect to each other is explained with examples.
  - 3. Behaviours that are of concern to individuals are discussed promptly and openly with those involved.
  - 4. Examples are given of how individual behaviour is modified and changed to support other team member's feelings and needs.
- Unit 3: Unit 3: Participate in building relations between team members and other stakeholders
  - 1. The importance of building relations between team members and stakeholders is explained with examples.
  - 2. Project stakeholders are identified and their needs are explained in terms of teamwork.
  - 3. Instances of building relations between team members and stakeholders are documented and implemented according to procedures.
  - 4. The importance of honouring commitments to stakeholders is explained with practical examples.
  - 5. Methods and techniques for building team coherence and spirit are identified and explained with practical examples.
  - 6. Feedback is provided on an ongoing basis which leads to constructive and productive working relationships.
- Unit 4: Unit 2: Collaborate with other team members to improve performance
  - 1. The importance of consultation and joint decision-making is explained with examples of how this affects team performance.
  - 2. Other team members are consulted for ideas relating to project work and joint decisions are made according to team needs.
  - 3. Other team members are worked with in order to achieve project objectives.
  - 4. Constructive, non-disruptive behaviours and how others are influenced positively are provided, described, and explained with examples.
  - 5. Situations that are a cause of conflict in a group are identified and a plan is made to minimise their negative effect on the team and project objectives.
- Unit 5: Unit 5: Use a variety of strategies to deal with potential or actual conflict in a project team
  - 1. The kinds of conflict that could arise in a project team are identified and strategies to deal with issues in a team are demonstrated in role-play situations or through discussion.
  - 2. Strategies for creating a positive working environment for a project team are explored and an indication is given of the role of the team leader/project manager in creating a positive work environment.
  - 3. Situations that hamper efficiency in a project team are identified and suggestions are made to improve these situations.
  - 4. Support systems available to the project team are identified and an indication is given of the learner's own role in being supportive and using a support system.

  - SpecCon Holdings (Pty) Ltd

Course 212 of 288
Course Name: Project Budget Preparation and Management
Course Description: This course introduces the principles and processes involved in estimating, preparing, monitoring, and controlling project costs. Emphasis is placed on documenting assumptions, obtaining approvals, tracking actuals against budget, identifying variances, and maintaining accurate financial records. By the end of the course, participants will be able to contribute effectively to project cost planning and control, supporting informed decision-making and financial discipline.
Course Overview: Every successful project rests on the foundation of sound budgeting. This course equips participants with the essential tools to estimate costs accurately, prepare detailed budgets, and maintain financial control throughout the project lifecycle, ensuring alignment with both performance and accountability standards.
Duration (minutes): 160
Units:
- Unit 1: Unit 3: Contribute to the monitoring and controlling of cost budget performance by maintaining records and communicating
  - 1. The cost budget is communicated in a manner that ensures all relevant parties are clear on its contents. 2. Actual costs against the budget elements are obtained and records are updated correctly. 3. Deviations of actual costs against budgeted costs are identified and communicated to higher authority. 4. Opportunities for corrective action or improvement are identified and communicated to relevant individuals/teams. 5. Financial records are maintained according to agreed standards and procedures.
- Unit 2: Unit 2: Participate in the preparation and production of a cost budget
  - 1. The elements of cost for each work element/package are estimated using agreed rules and procedures. 2. A cost budget is documented in the agreed format and within agreed time frames. 3. Approval is obtained for the budget from higher authority in accordance with established standards and procedures. 5.   - 1. The work elements are identified and extracted from the data. 2. Cost types (elements) are identified and agreed with financial and/or project management authorities. 3. Unit costs to be used for cost estimating are agreed upon with the relevant authority. 4. The resource requirements for work elements are determined in terms of type, quantity, and unit cost, and documented in the agreed format.

Course 222 of 288
Course Name: Using Information From Texts
Course Description: In this course, students will explore Interpret and Use Information from Texts, a comprehensive programme aimed at developing learners’ ability to read, interpret, and critically engage with a variety of written and visual texts. The course begins by building core comprehension skills, including identifying unfamiliar words or signs and determining their meanings through syntax, contextual clues, and analytical strategies. Learners will explore how ambiguous words function within context, how to distinguish main ideas from supporting details, and how to summarise or paraphrase information accurately. Visual literacy is also addressed, with a focus on recognising the purpose and impact of visual and graphic elements. As the course progresses, learners will evaluate the reliability and potential bias of text sources, analyse the attitudes and intentions behind messages, and examine techniques used to influence audiences, such as language choice, omission of material, and tone. The course also covers practical applications, such as responding appropriately to instructions and requests, and selecting suitable text types, formats, and levels of formality. Finally, learners will explore how language, symbols, signs, and visual elements contribute to shaping and supporting a particular point of view. This course is ideal for individuals seeking to enhance their critical reading and comprehension skills for academic, personal, or professional purposes.
Course Overview: This course is designed to develop and strengthen learners’ abilities to critically read, analyse and interpret a range of texts. It equips participants with the skills to identify key ideas, understand unfamiliar vocabulary using contextual strategies, and evaluate visual and written information. Learners will also explore the influence of bias, language choice, and presentation techniques in shaping meaning and purpose. By the end of the course, learners will be able to engage with different text types effectively, whether for instruction, information, or persuasion.
Duration (minutes): 160
Units:
- Unit 1: Unit 3: Respond to selected texts in a manner appropriate to the context
  - 1. Instructions and requests are acted upon.
  - 2. The text type, format and register used are on the appropriate level of formality.
- Unit 2: Unit 4: Explore and explain how language structures and features may influence a reader or viewer
  - 1. The choice of words/signs, language usage, symbols, pictures and tone/sign size and pace are described in terms of how a point of view is shaped or supported.
- Unit 3: Unit 2: Use strategies for extracting implicit messages in texts
  - 1. The source of the text is identified and discussed in terms of reliability and possible bias.
  - 2. Attitudes, beliefs and intentions are explored to determine the point of view expressed either directly or indirectly.
  - 3. Techniques are explored and explained in terms of purpose and audience.
  - 4. Promotion of, or support for, a particular line of thought/cause is identified and explained concerning the selection or omission of materials.
- Unit 4: Unit 1: Use a range of reading and/or viewing strategies to understand the literal meaning of specific texts
  - 1. Unfamiliar words/signs are identified. Their meanings are correctly determined by using knowledge of syntax, word-attack skills/sign parameter/analysis skills, and contextual clues.
  - 2. Different options for the meanings of ambiguous words are tested, and selected meanings are correct in relation to the context.
  - 3. The main ideas are separated from supporting evidence and paraphrased or summarised.
  - 4. The purpose of visual and/or graphic representations in texts are recognised and explained.
  - 5. Features of visual texts are explained in relation to the way they impact meaning.

The course progresses to cover the development of actionable work plans, allocation of tasks, and timeframes for project execution. Learners will also explore proactive management techniques such as efficient meetings, communication processes, and administrative planning. By the end of the course, participants will have a clear, practical framework to implement sustainable time management strategies within their specific work environment.
Course Overview: Effective time management is essential to organisational success, team productivity, and personal balance. This course provides a structured approach to assessing, planning, and improving how time is used at both individual and departmental levels. Through an exploration of proven techniques, key principles such as prioritisation, delegation, and the 80/20 rule, learners will develop the capability to manage tasks and resources efficiently. The course addresses how to identify time wasters, streamline work processes, and align daily activities with broader organisational goals, ultimately enabling more strategic and value-driven use of time.

  - 2. Emphasis is placed on proactive measures such as efficient information flow, efficient meeting planning and management and administrative procedures in the daily work processes of the department/division/section to minimise time wasting.
  - 3. Plans are implemented once all involved are informed of their roles, duties, and functions.

  - 3. Prioritising as a technique to manage the work of a team/group/section is explored concerning the work of the specific group. A decision is made as to which tasks are of greater priority for the group.
  - 4. The principle of balance between the various aspects of one’s life is understood in terms of creating time for them all to optimise one’s life.

  - 2. The objectives are translated into work plans for the department/division/section.
  - 3. The key activities required to complete a specific project are identified and all tasks and work procedures are analysed and assigned to a specific time frame.
  - 4. Persons to whom tasks can be delegated are identified and included in the plan.
  - 5. Plans eliminate and/ or damage time wasters in the department/ division/ section.
  - 6. Tasks are prioritised in terms of urgency and importance for the department/ division section/ organisation.

Course 251 of 288
Course Name: Empowering Team Members
Course Description: The Empowering Team Members course is designed to equip participants with the knowledge and strategies needed to enhance individual and collective performance within a team. The course begins by identifying team roles, duties, and performance expectations, setting a clear foundation for individual accountability. Learners will then explore methods of providing constructive feedback, recognising achievements, and addressing performance gaps while fostering trust and respect within the team. Participants will gain practical skills in inclusive decision-making by learning how to involve team members in discussions, generate and evaluate solutions collaboratively, and build consensus through open dialogue. Delegation is another key focus, with detailed guidance on assigning tasks effectively, communicating expectations clearly, granting appropriate authority, and ensuring follow-up through consistent feedback and reporting systems. The course concludes with a strong emphasis on reflection and improvement. Learners will review decisions and outcomes in group settings, identify successes and failures, and adjust plans accordingly to meet objectives. By encouraging shared responsibility and continuous development, this course lays the groundwork for empowered, proactive, and resilient teams.
Course Overview: In today’s fast-paced and collaborative workplace, empowering team members is essential to achieving sustained organisational success. This course provides a structured approach to fostering a high-performance team environment where individuals understand their roles, actively contribute to decision-making, and take ownership of delegated responsibilities. Through a practical exploration of communication, collaboration, delegation, and reflection, learners will develop the skills to nurture a supportive team culture where each member is recognised as a valued contributor. The course focuses on building mutual trust, encouraging innovation, and promoting accountability to ensure the effective delivery of departmental and organisational objectives.
Duration (minutes): 180
Units:
- Unit 1: Unit 1: Recognising team member performance
  - 1. (incl. 1.2) Recognising team member performance.
  - 2. The role, duties, and responsibilities of each team member.
  - 3. (cont.) Additional examples of roles of team members.
  - 4. Giving feedback to team members.
  - 5. Giving feedback effectively.
  - 6. Dealing with team members effectively.
- Unit 2: Unit 4: Reviewing decisions and performance of delegated tasks
  - 1. (incl. 4.2) Reviewing decisions and performance of delegated tasks.
  - 2. Reviewing delegated tasks.
- Unit 3: Unit 2: Encouragement of participation in decision-making
  - 1.(incl. 2.2 & 2.3) Encouragement of participation in decision-making.
  - 2. Providing alternatives, evaluating and selecting one alternative for implementation.
- Unit 4: Unit 3: Delegation of tasks
  - 3.1 (incl. 3.2 & 3.3) Delegation of tasks.
  - 3.4 (incl. 3.5) Decision-making authority.
  - 3.6 Establishing an Information-Sharing System.
  - 3.7 Monitoring the successful completion of delegated tasks and using performance as a means of ongoing development.
  - 3.7 (cont.) Recognition of achievement of delegated tasks.

Course 252 of 288
Course Name: Understanding Different Business Environments
Course Description: This course introduces learners to the various forms of business organisations and how they function within different sectors. It explores the common business activities across sectors, highlights key players, and categorises their offerings. Learners will gain a foundational understanding of trade and marketing principles, the role of specific sectors in the national economy, and how value chains drive operations. The course also examines the purpose and influence of professional bodies and regulatory authorities, as well as tools for evaluating competitiveness, such as SWOT analysis. By the end, learners will be able to assess organisations within their environments with greater clarity and insight.
Course Overview: Understanding the diversity and complexity of today’s business environments is essential for anyone pursuing a career in commerce or industry. This course provides learners with insight into different types of organisations, their roles, and their interactions within broader economic and regulatory frameworks. It highlights how organisations operate, trade, and compete, and how they are influenced by market principles, professional bodies, and external forces.
Duration (minutes): 150
Units:
- Unit 1: Unit 4: Discuss the market position of a selected organisation in the relevant sub-sector
  - 1. A list of 10 of the products and/or services marketed by a selected organisation is tabulated and compared with equivalent products and/or services of competitor organisations.
  - 2. A description of the organisation's current competitive position is given, based on available audited data.
  - 3. The strengths and weaknesses of the organisation are compared with those of its two major competitors.
  - 4. The opportunities and threats facing the organisation are explained with reference to the external environment.
- Unit 2: Unit 2: Demonstrate an understanding of the concept of a market as applied to a selected business sector
  - 1. The principles of trade that define markets are identified at a basic level of understanding.
  - 2. The basic principles for the marketing of products are differentiated from the basic principles for the marketing of services.
  - 3. The role of a selected business sector in the national economy is explained in the context of the business environment.
  - 4. The value chain describing the way business is conducted in the sector is explained, illustrating with examples.
- Unit 3: Unit 3: Identify and describe the role of professional bodies in a selected business sector
  - 1. The reasons for the existence of professional bodies, associations, and regulatory authorities within or affecting this sector are explained in the context of the roles that they play.
  - 2. Three professional bodies, associations, or regulatory authorities are identified for each of the sub-sectors.
  - 3. The benefits of belonging to a selected professional body, association, or regulatory authority within the sector are outlined from the perspective of both the organisation and the individual.
  - 4. Information about two of the professional bodies, associations, or regulatory authorities is accessed from its website or an industry publication.
- Unit 4: Unit 1: Explain the structure and roles of different types of organisations within their own industry in SA
  - 1. The various types of organisations are named and explained using the terminology accepted within their own industry.
  - 2. The roles of the different types of organisations are explained in the context of the business environment.
  - 3. Business activities common to all organisations within the sector are identified and listed from readily available information.
  - 4. Two examples of companies in each business sub-sector are identified from advertisements in the media.
  - 5. Four of the main players in the field are identified and the kind of products or services offered by each are listed and categorised according to purpose.

Course 253 of 288
Course Name: Stock and Fixed Asset Management
Course Description: This unit standard is intended for managers of small businesses and junior managers of business units in larger organisations. It provides the background necessary to understand the management of assets and stock in a business unit. The term business unit in this unit standard implies a small business, cost centre, section or department. Junior managers include, but are not limited to team leaders, supervisors, first-line managers and section heads. The positioner term is used to describe the first level of management in an organisation at which an employee has other employees reporting to him/her. The qualifying learner is capable of differentiating between fixed assets and stock in a business unit. Explaining the influence that stock management can have on the profitability of a business. Explaining the management of fixed assets in a business unit. Applying the basic principles of stock and fixed asset management to a business unit.
Course Overview: This unit standard is intended for managers of small businesses and junior managers of business units in larger organisations. It provides the background necessary to understand the management of assets and stock in a business unit.
Duration (minutes): 120
Units:
- Unit 1: Unit 1: Differentiate between fixed assets and stock in a business unit
  - 1. The concepts of fixed assets and stock are explained with examples
  - 2. The different fixed assets in a business unit are identified and an indication is given of the purpose of each asset in the business unit
  - 3. Stock in a business unit is identified and a list is compiled of the stock usually needed in a business unit
  - 4. The problems that occur in a specific business unit if there is insufficient stock are indicated, and a plan is compiled to ensure that the required stock is available when needed
  - 5. Problems if a business unit has too much stock are explained, and an indication is given of how stockpiling impacts on the bottom line of the business
- Unit 2: Unit 3:  Explain the management of fixed assets in a business unit
  - 1. The fixed assets in a business unit are identified from a balance sheet
  - 2. The asset register for a business unit is updated for three case studies
  - 3. The valuation of assets in a business unit is explained with reference to depreciation and investment
  - 4. Reasons for depreciation are explained with examples and an indication is given of the purpose of depreciation
- Unit 3: Unit 2: Explain the influence that stock management can have on the profitability of a business
  - 1. The need for stock control is explained with reference to fraud, theft, carelessness and ensuring sufficient stock
  - 2. The different ways of managing stock are explained with reference to records and stocktaking
  - 3. The importance of quality, quantity, time, price and source in managing stock is explained with examples
  - 4. The rate of stock turnover for a business unit is calculated and an indication is given of how knowing turnover assists in planning
  - 5. An Economic Ordering Quantity Model (EOQ) model is explained and applied to a business unit to calculate the optimum stock level for three items in a business unit
- Unit 4: Unit 4: Apply the basic principles of stock and fixed asset management to a business unit
  - 1. The risk associated with the management of stock in a business unit is identified and quantified in terms of probability and severity
  - 2. The risk associated with the management of fixed assets in a business unit is identified and quantified in terms of probability and severity.
  - 3. A system for managing stock in a business unit is applied with reference to ensuring sufficient stock, control of costs and the value of the stock.
  - 4. A plan is designed to minimize the risk associated with fixed assets in a business unit

Course 254 of 288
Course Name: Administrative Record Management
Course Description: The Manage Administration Records course provides a structured approach to handling confidential information, securing documents, and implementing effective record-keeping systems. You will learn to develop and control office stationery plans, monitor stock levels, and apply shrinkage control measures. Additionally, the course covers procedures for identifying and reporting non-conformances, ensuring compliance with company policies. By the end of the course, you will be able to maintain organised and secure administrative records that support smooth business operations.
Course Overview: This course equips learners with the skills to manage administrative records effectively, ensuring confidentiality, accuracy, and compliance with organisational policies.
Duration (minutes): 180
Units:
- Unit 1: Unit 2: Control and evaluate ordering and distribution of office stationery
  - 1. A plan is presented to effectively control office stationery policies, procedures, and strategies.
  - 2. Plans are developed on how to monitor, maintain, and improve stock levels in accordance with organisational requirements.
  - 3. Effective shrinkage controls are developed and implemented for an organisation.
  - 4. Evidence of accurate reports is produced reflecting stationery movements for a given period.
  - 5. The control of the administration system and procedures is explained and applied to ensure effective administering of stationery.
  - 6. Documentation used for the control of stationery in an accurate, complete way, which complies with requirements is explained to employees.
  - 7. Effective stationery control procedures, systems, and follow-up actions are evaluated and explained.
- Unit 2: Unit 1: Control and deal with confidential information and documents
  - 1. Confidential information is defined and described for a specific organisation.
  - 2. The system and procedures used for dealing with confidential information is explained with examples.
  - 3. Documents are secured in an appropriate manner and within an agreed time frame.
  - 4. Utmost care is taken to avoid compromising any relevant stakeholder.
- Unit 3: Unit 3: Implement control measures with individuals
  - 1. Contracted control measures are implemented and non-conformances are identified for reporting to persons with the authority to deal with them.
  - 2. Non-conformances are recorded and corrective actions negotiated according to organisational requirements.
  - 3. Reported non-conformance is handled in accordance with organisational policies and procedures and is duly recorded.

Course 255 of 288
Course Name: Analysing Media Impact on Business Sectors
Course Description: This course focuses on analysing media-reported developments and understanding their potential impact on business sectors and industries. You will explore how political, technological, environmental, and economic changes can shape industries and the business strategies needed to adapt. Through evaluating current events, innovations, and controversial issues, you will gain insights into how businesses can respond to these shifts and maintain competitive advantage in a dynamic environment.
Course Overview: This course teaches you to analyse media-reported developments and evaluate their impact on business sectors and industries. You will explore political, technological, environmental, and economic changes, and learn how businesses can respond and adapt to these challenges.
Duration (minutes): 100
Units:
- Unit 1: Unit 3: Analyse proposed business or industrial development that could impact on the physical environment
  - 1. Articles and reports on events, both global and national, on proposed business or industrial developments that could impact the physical environment, are collected over at least 6 months.
  - 2. The articles are summarised, showing insight into how the reported events could impact the physical environment in South Africa and internationally.
  - 3. The events are summarised in a table and ranked to indicate the relative impact of each event on the physical environment.
  - 4. Controversial issues related to a business or industrial development are analysed and own views are expressed and substantiated in plain language.
  - 5. The sustainability of the proposed development is discussed from the point of view of both the developer and the environment.
- Unit 2: Unit 1: Analyse articles and reports from current print and electronic material
  - 1. Articles and reports on events, both global and national, that could result in changes in a specific business sector or industry are collected over at least 6 months.
  - 2. The articles are summarised, showing insight into how the reported events could impact a business sector or industry in South  Africa and internationally.
  - 3. The events are summarised in a table and ranked to indicate the relative importance of each event for a business sector or industry in South Africa.
  - 4. Controversial issues related to a business sector or industry are analysed, and their views are expressed and substantiated in plain language.
  - 5. Current events in the political and legislative environments are interpreted, and an indication of their possible impact on a specific business sector or industry is given.
- Unit 3: Unit 2: Demonstrate knowledge and understanding of the latest technological innovations and developments
  - 1. Innovations or developments in technology that could affect a specific business sector or industry are described, and an indication is given of how the innovation or technology could impact the business sector or industry.
  - 2. The possible impact of the innovation on a specific business sector or industry is explained, and an indication is given of the possible time frame before the technology becomes readily available.
  - 3. The pros and cons of the innovations or technologies are investigated and summarised in a table.
  - 4. A recommendation is made as to whether the innovations should be further investigated and how they could add value to a particular organisation.
- Unit 4: Unit 4: Analyse issues in the media relating to labour that could impact on a business sector or industry
  - 1. Wage negotiation in specific sectors is discussed with reference to increases in salaries and trends in the sector. 2. The sustainability of developments in a business sector or industry is analysed in relation to ongoing employment. 3. Incidents involving the withholding of labour and other protests are analysed to identify the outcomes of the action. 4. The role of the unions in a specific business sector or industry is identified and an indication is given of the issues addressed in their deliberations. 5. Articles relating to unemployment and job losses in a business sector or industry are examined, and possible reasons for a trend are given. 6. The impact of HIV/AIDS on a business sector or industry is determined from reports in the media, and an indication is given of what, if anything, the business sector or industry is doing to manage the impact of the pandemic in the sector.

Course 256 of 288
Course Name: Managing Office Supplies
Course Description: This course focuses on the systematic management of office supplies to ensure operational efficiency and compliance with organisational standards. Learners will explore techniques for tracking supply levels, evaluating processes, addressing discrepancies, and implementing improvements. Emphasis is placed on proactive monitoring, effective control strategies, and aligning supply management with broader organisational needs.
Course Overview: Beneath routine operations lies the unseen rhythm of supply, monitored, adjusted, and refined to sustain the flow of work.
Duration (minutes): 150
Units:
- Unit 1: Unit 3: Monitor and control the distribution of office supplies
  - 1. Distribution procedures are identified, set, and communicated.
  - 2. Office supply requests are received and recorded.
  - 3. Office supplies are distributed within agreed timeframes.
  - 4. Office supply distribution procedures are followed.
  - 5. Areas of non-conformance are identified and highlighted.
  - 6. Remedial action is taken to rectify office supply distribution processes and procedures.
- Unit 2: Unit 1: Monitor office supply levels
  - 1. Office supplies levels are identified and recorded.
  - 2. Office supply levels are ascertained and compared to the required levels.
  - 3. Records are checked for compliance with organisational requirements.
  - 4. Remedial action is taken to rectify office supply levels.
- Unit 3: Unit 2: Maintain office supplies processes and procedures
  - 1. Office supply processes and procedures are monitored and evaluated.
  - 2. Out-of-line situations are identified and highlighted.
  - 3. Remedial action is taken to bring office supply processes and procedures back in line.
  - 4. Areas for improvement are identified and recommendations are made by the authorised individuals.

Course 257 of 288
Course Name: Administrative Procedure Development
Course Description: The Administrative Procedure Development course equips learners with the skills to establish, manage, and improve administrative systems in a business environment. You will learn to identify key administrative needs, allocate resources, and develop structured procedures that align with company policies and legal regulations. Additionally, the course covers confidentiality protocols, access controls, and the creation of a formalised administrative manual. By the end of this course, you will be able to design efficient administrative processes that enhance organisational effectiveness and compliance.
Course Overview: This unit standard is for all persons involved in administration in commercial or non-commercial organisations and who have the responsibility of developing administrative procedures to make the administrative component of the organisation more effective and efficient and so aid the organisation to attain its mission, vision and objectives.
Duration (minutes): 170
Units:
- Unit 1: Unit 1: Demonstrate an understanding of the administrative systems required
  - 1. A list of all administrative systems required in a selected business environment is compiled including client-filing systems, staff administrative systems, and business systems.
  - 2. The elements and usage of each system are described in relation to the company and legal requirements.
  - 3. Resources such as staff, information technology, office space, and management requirements for the development of these administrative systems are listed, and ways of finding these resources are identified in a specific business institution.
- Unit 2: Unit  3: Develop systems to keep administrative information at the required level of confidentiality
  - 1. Administrative information, which should be kept confidential, is identified in accordance with legal, company and industry requirements and practices. 2. Systems are developed to keep administrative information and records confidential and maintain the secrecy of such information as required legally and by the company. 3. Mandates for access to confidential information are identified for administrative and other staff according to their job role.
- Unit 3: Unit  4: Develop policies and procedures on administrative systems and write them into a manual
  - 1. Procedures, which are in alignment with legislative and organisational requirements, are developed for the administrative systems.
  - 2. The procedure for each element of the administration system is explained to employees in line with the policies developed.
  - 3. The policies and procedures are collated into a written manual in company-specific format.
- Unit 4: Unit  2: Develop and update administrative systems in a specific business environment
  - 1. The administrative requirements are identified to meet the specific needs of a selected business organisation. 2. The identified administrative systems are developed in accordance with the organisational and legal requirements. 3. The administrative systems and procedures identified are presented to management and staff for approval. 4. Feedback is obtained from management and staff regarding the suitability of the systems on specifically designed feedback forms. 5. Agreed changes are made to the systems.
- Unit 5: Author
  - SpecCon Holdings (Pty) Ltd

Course 258 of 288
Course Name: Basic Office Research
Course Description: This unit standard provides learners with the essential knowledge and skills required to plan and conduct basic research within their own organisation. It covers fundamental research methods, including defining research objectives, designing research strategies, and collecting and analysing data. Learners will gain practical experience in applying these techniques to address specific issues or opportunities within their organisation. The course aims to enhance their ability to generate valuable insights, make informed decisions, and contribute to organisational development through effective research practices.
Course Overview: This unit standard introduces the knowledge and skills needed to plan and conduct basic research within the learner`s own organisation.
Duration (minutes): 160
Units:
- Unit 1: Unit 3: Analyse the data obtained from the research
  - 1. A list of five data analysis techniques is compiled, describing the suitability of each for the data obtained and the research topic in question.
  - 2. A particular analysis technique is selected based on the most appropriate for the data obtained and the type of research carried out.
  - 3. The data is analysed correctly using the selected analysis technique.
  - 4. Only the relevant findings are selected for presentation in the report.
- Unit 2: Unit 2: Gather and collate data relevant to the research question or problem
  - 1. The data is gathered according to the methodology described in the plan.
  - 2. The data is collated according to the methodology described in the plan.
  - 3. Where it has been necessary to change any part of the plan, reasons for the change are justified in writing.
  - 4. The data recorded in raw format and collated format.
- Unit 3: Unit 5: Evaluate the effectiveness and utility of the research
  - 1. The effectiveness of the selected techniques is discussed with reference to the purpose of the research being carried out.
  - 2. The utility of the research is discussed with reference to the stated purpose and design.
- Unit 4: Unit 1: Plan a simple research project
  - 1. The need for and the purpose of the research is clearly identified and confirmed in writing with the key stakeholders.
  - 2. The scope of the research is delineated after consultation with the key stakeholders.
  - 3. A list of at least five qualitative and quantitative research methodologies is compiled, describing the suitability of each for the research topic in question.
  - 4. A particular methodology is selected based on the most appropriate design for the research in question.
  - 5. A research plan, describing the purpose, the question or problem to be solved, the expected outcome, the methodology and any schedules, questionnaires or models that will be used is formulated according to a selected published model.
- Unit 5: Unit 4: Prepare and present a report and recommendations based on the findings of the research
  - 1. The report includes all the elements of the plan, as well as the collated data, the analysis, the findings, a discussion with reference to published works relating to the topic, the recommendations, a conclusion and references.
  - 2. The report contains appropriate diagrams, graphs or charts that serve to illustrate and enhance comprehension of the points being made.
  - 3. The report links researched findings to published data in an integrated manner.
  - 4. The format of the report is based on a company specific template designed for the purpose.

Course 259 of 288
Course Name: Plan and Prepare Meeting Communications
Course Description: This course provides a practical and structured approach to planning and preparing meeting communications. Learners will explore the advantages of a well-constructed agenda, how to arrange agenda items logically, and identify appropriate sources for agenda matters. The course also covers producing agendas in the required format and timeframe, as well as the different types of minutes, their importance, and methods of accurate recording. Learners will examine distribution processes, including lists, methods, and reasons for sharing minutes. Finally, the course develops essential skills for taking and producing accurate minutes that support decision-making and accountability. By the end of the course, participants will be able to confidently manage meeting communications with professionalism and clarity.
Course Overview: Effective meetings rely on clear communication, structured planning, and accurate documentation. This course equips learners with the skills to create well-organised agendas, take precise minutes, and ensure timely distribution of meeting communications. By focusing on preparation, structure, and record-keeping, learners will gain the tools needed to support professional, productive, and outcome-driven meetings.
Duration (minutes): 180
Units:
- Unit 1: Unit 3: Take minutes of meetings
  - 1. Resources required for minute taking are identified, listed, and explained.
  - 2. Items to be included in minutes of the meeting are listed and explained.
  - 3. Attendees to the meeting are identified.
  - 4. The characteristics of good minutes are identified and explained.
  - 5. Minutes are concise and accurate and reflect proceedings.
  - 6. Minutes are produced and distributed in the required format and time frame.
- Unit 2: Unit 1: Demonstrate an understanding of the agenda of meetings
  - 1. The advantages of a well-constructed agenda are explained.
  - 2. Matters on the agenda appear in a logical and systematically order.
  - 3. Sources of agenda matters are identified and explained.
  - 4. An agenda is produced in the required format and time frame.
- Unit 3: Unit 2: Explain the purpose and objective of minutes of meetings
  - 1. Types of minutes are identified and explained.
  - 2. The importance of accurate recording and producing of minutes is explained.
  - 3. The distribution list is described.
  - 4. Methods of distributing minutes are explained.
  - 5. The reasons for distributing minutes promptly are explained.

Course 260 of 288
Course Name: Managing Workplace Conflicts

Units:

  - 2. (incl. 2.2.1) Useful steps to be taken to manage conflict

  - 2.3     Different stages of conflict

  - 1. Introduction - methods available to resolve conflict in terms of the Labour Relations Act
  - 2. The most appropriate strategy to resolve a particular conflict
  - 3. Action plans for conflict resolution
  - 4. The role organisational policies and procedures play in preventing/resolving conflicts.
- Unit 3: Unit 4: The attributes of an effective conflict manager
  - 1. Personal attributes of a good conflict manager
  - 2. Conducting a skills audit
  - 3. The negative attributes which should be avoided or controlled by an effective conflict manager.
- Unit 4: Unit 1:  The main sources of conflict
  - 1. Possible sources of conflict
  - 2. Positive and negative characteristics of conflict in the workplace
  - 3. Conflict which may arise in personality types.

Course 261 of 288
Course Name: Manage Diversity to Add Value in the Workplace
Course Description: This course equips learners with the knowledge and practical tools needed to manage a diverse workforce effectively. It begins by defining diversity across multiple dimensions — such as culture, values, language, and education—and explores the challenges, including bias and discrimination, that can arise within diverse teams. Learners will investigate how diversity impacts relationships, and how it can be harnessed to foster innovation, meet varied team and client needs, and unlock new opportunities. The course also focuses on leadership strategies that encourage open expression, build common ground, and resolve conflict constructively. Through real-world scenarios and reflective practice, learners will develop the skills to promote inclusion, manage difference, and lead diverse teams with empathy and clarity.
Course Overview: Diversity can be a source of strength or strain — depending on how it's managed. This course explores how inclusive leadership and thoughtful engagement can transform diverse teams into powerful, collaborative units that drive meaningful outcomes.
Duration (minutes): 290
Units:
- Unit 1: Unit 1: Diversity in the workplace
  - 1.  Definition of key terms.
  - 2.  Definition of diversity.
  - 3.  Multiple generations, multiple work skills and styles.
  - 4.  Diversity as a potential source of discrimination.
  - 5.  The implications of diversity for external and internal relationships.
  - 6.  (cont'd) A.
  - 7.  (cont'd) C.
  - 8.  Cultural biases, stereotypes and perceptions and their influence on diversity.
  - 9.  Suggestions to facilitate cross-cultural communication.
  - 10.  Be aware of your own potential biases and prejudices.
  - 11.  Perception and diversity.
  - 12.  Persons perception and workforce diversity.
  - 13.  Embracing a diverse gender workplace.
- Unit 2: Unit 2: The reality of diversity and its value in the unit
  - 1.  Introduction.
  - 2.  Benefits of diversity in employees and clients for an organisation.
  - 3.  Ways of utilising the diverse talents, attitudes, and values of employees.
  - 4.  Components of attitudes.
  - 5.  Perspectives.
  - 6.  Reflection of the community.
  - 7.  Ways of meeting the diverse needs of employees.
  - 8.  Ways of meeting the diverse needs of clients with a range of products and services.
  - 9.  Reflection.
  - 10.  Examples.
  - 11.  Encouraging diverse viewpoints in meetings.
- Unit 3: Unit 4:  Dealing with disagreements and conflict arising from diversity in the unit
  - 1.  Introduction.
  - 2.  Recognising and dealing with all incidents of conflict and disagreement.
  - 3.  Using disagreements and conflict as opportunities for learning.
  - 4.  Identifying and managing all cases of discrimination and discriminatory practices.
- Unit 4: Unit 3: Managing team members
  - 1.  Introduction.
  - 2.  Tools for managers to overcome communication barriers.
  - 3.  Creation of mutual respect and trust.
  - 4.  Common beliefs, values, interests, and attitudes that will serve as a basis for leading the team.
  - 5.  Encouraging the expression of diverse viewpoints.
  - 6.  Sensitivity towards and understanding of diversity.

Units:

Course 263 of 288
Course Name: Maintenance of Office Equipment
Course Description: Learners will be working towards obtaining a national qualification at Level 3 or will be employed in an administrative role within a Small, Medium, and Micro Business (SMME) environment. Achieving competence in this standard will enhance their current job performance and improve their prospects for future employment. This qualification is designed to provide practical skills and knowledge relevant to administrative tasks, adding significant value to their professional capabilities. For those in the SMME sector, mastering these skills will not only contribute to their effectiveness in their current roles but also increase their attractiveness to potential employers, thereby broadening their career opportunities.

Course 268 of 288
Course Name: Understanding HIV/AIDS in the Workplace
Course Description: This comprehensive course provides foundational knowledge of HIV and AIDS, from understanding the immune system and stages of infection to the latest testing methods and treatment options. Learners will explore modes of transmission, behavioural risks, and the social and economic impact of the disease, particularly in workplace and community settings. The course also unpacks policy frameworks, workers’ rights, and the role of education in reducing stigma. With a strong emphasis on prevention, wellness, and compassionate engagement, the course empowers participants to respond proactively to the challenges of HIV and AIDS through informed personal choices and organisational action.
Course Overview: This course empowers individuals with essential knowledge and practical tools to understand, prevent, and respond to the impact of HIV and AIDS. It supports informed decision-making, encourages responsible behaviour, and promotes a compassionate, proactive approach in both community and workplace settings.
Duration (minutes): 230
Units:
- Unit 1: Unit 4: Know what guidelines and assistance are available to support workers with HIV/AIDS
  - 1. A company policy on HIV/AIDS or the National Department of Health's document "Guidelines for developing a workplace policy and programme" is accessed and evidence of knowledge is provided in the form of a summary.
  - 2. The possible problems that a worker with HIV/AIDS could encounter are listed with suggestions as to what the learner himself/herself could do to create a caring situation in the workplace.
  - 3. The importance of employers playing a proactive role in addressing the AIDS pandemic are known and understood and ways in which a company can create a caring environment for workers with HIV/AIDS are suggested for a familiar context.
  - 4. The availability of HIV/AIDS prevention and wellness programmes provided by medical schemes, organisations and other bodies is known and an explanation is given on how to access them.
  - 5. The treatment options available to a person with HIV/AIDS are known and a table is compiled indicating which treatment is available locally.
  - 6. The rights of all workers in respect of HIV/AIDS are known and their responsibilities are understood dealing with the pandemic.
  - 7. The universal precautions are known and applied in the work environment.
  - 8. A code of behaviour in the workplace is drafted.
  - 9. A presentation is created to help address the stigma surrounding HIV/AIDS and the importance of employers playing a proactive role in dealing with HIV/AIDS.
- Unit 2: Unit 2: Know and understand how HIV/AIDS is transmitted
  - 1. The effect of body fluids on the transmission of HIV is outlined at a basic level of understanding.
  - 2. Sex is identified as the most common way in which HIV is transmitted and other ways in which HIV is transmitted are listed with an indication of the conditions necessary for transmission.
  - 3. How mother to child transmission can occur are listed and the implication of a pregnant woman/girl having unprotected sex is indicated for both the mother and the unborn child.
  - 4. Actions that an HIV positive mother can take to lower the risk of infection to the child and prolong the onset of AIDS in herself are presented in a poster to promote wellness.
  - 5. The dangers of drug abuse and behaviour that could result in HIV transmission are explained with suggestions for limiting transmission.
  - 6. Precautions used in South Africa to ensure that blood product is HIV free are outlined at a basic level of understanding.
- Unit 3: Unit 5: Know and understand the implications of the HIV/AIDS pandemic
  - 1. The needs of AIDS orphans are outlined with reference, at a basic level of understanding, to the burden of a large number of orphans on society and the economy.
  - 2. The effect of a population composed mainly of children and the aged on the economy and the State is outlined at a basic level of understanding.
  - 3. The need for medical care for people with HIV/AIDS and the implications for employers and the State are discussed at a basic level of understanding.
  - 4. The effect of HIV/AIDS on the workforce and family income is discussed at a basic level of understanding.
  - 5. The effect of HIV/AIDS for an organisation are discussed at a basic level of understanding.
  - 6. The implications of HIV/AIDS for a specific workplace are discussed at a basic level of understanding.
  - 7. The implications of HIV and AIDS for an industry sub-sector are discussed at a basic level of understanding.
- Unit 4: Unit 3: Know what behaviour is safe and what behaviour carries the risk of HIV transmission
  - 1. The relationship between human behaviour and HIV/AIDS is outlined at a basic level of understanding.
  - 2. Ways in which the individual can avoid contracting or spreading HIV/AIDS are named with an indication of how own behaviour can reduce the risk of infection.
  - 3. Examples of behaviour that carry a risk of contracting HIV/AIDS are named and classified according to whether they carry a high, medium or low risk.
  - 4. Situations that have the potential to spread HIV/AIDS in the workplace are discussed and rated in terms of high, medium and low risk.
  - 5. Fears and common misunderstandings about the transmission of HIV/AIDS are described in the context of the workplace.
  - 6. The reasons are given why certain behaviours and activities carry a low risk of infection.
  - 7. The role of sexually transmitted diseases (STDs) in the transmission of the HIV is known and understood and an indication is given of how untreated STDs greatly increase the risk of transmission.
- Unit 5: Unit 1: Know and understand HIV/AIDS and its effects on the human immune system
  - 1. The terms HIV and AIDS are known and explained at a basic level of understanding.
  - 2. How the immune system works is explained regarding the role of antibodies in the immune system.
  - 3. An indication is given as to how HIV attacks the immune system.
  - 4. The concept of a window period is explained regarding the Elisa test.
  - 5. The concept that the Elisa test tests for antibodies is known and an indication is given of the implications that this has in terms of the window period and the use of vaccinations.
  - 6. The fact that all babies born to HIV/AIDS mothers initially test positive for HIV is known and reasons are given to explain why these test results change over time.
  - 7. The concept of Voluntary Counselling and Testing (VCT) is explained with reference to the role of the Rapid Test and confirmation by the Elisa test.
  - 8. The effects of HIV infection are explained including the ability of infected persons to perform work and the importance of lifestyle changes to boost the immune system and prevent reinfection.
  - 9. The importance of pre and post-test counselling is known and understood, and the implications of HIV testing for an individual are discussed in terms of making a personal decision to take an AIDS test.
  - 10. The stages of the disease are outlined with an example of what happens at each stage from infection with HIV to full-blown AIDS and death.
  - 11. The chances of a person surviving with AIDS are discussed regarding the latest views on medication and the costs of the drugs.

Course 269 of 288
Course Name: Data Checking Assessment
Course Description: This assessment is designed to evaluate your proficiency in verifying and ensuring the accuracy and integrity of data. In today's data-driven world, the ability to meticulously check and validate information is essential for making informed decisions and maintaining data quality.

Throughout this assessment, you will encounter a series of tasks and exercises that will test your data-checking skills. You can expect to encounter the following elements:

Data Validation: You will be presented with datasets, spreadsheets, or databases containing various types of information. Your task will be to examine the data for inconsistencies, errors, or anomalies, and identify and rectify any inaccuracies.

Data Completeness: Assessing your ability to ensure that all required fields or data points are present and properly filled. You will need to carefully review the data to identify any missing information and take appropriate actions to address the gaps.

Data Formatting: You will work with data that requires proper formatting and adherence to specific guidelines or standards. Your task will involve checking for correct data types, formatting rules, and adherence to naming conventions.

Cross-referencing and Comparisons: Evaluating your capability to cross-check data from multiple sources or datasets to ensure consistency and accuracy. This may involve comparing data across different systems, documents, or periods.

Error Identification and Correction: Testing your ability to identify errors such as duplicate entries, incorrect calculations, or inconsistent data. You will be required to accurately locate these errors and take appropriate measures to correct them.

Data Integrity: Assessing your understanding of data integrity principles, including maintaining data accuracy, consistency, and reliability. You will be expected to identify and resolve issues that may compromise data integrity, such as data duplication or unauthorised modifications.

Attention to Detail: Emphasising the importance of being meticulous and thorough in your data-checking process. This assessment will evaluate your ability to spot even the smallest discrepancies or inconsistencies within the data.

By completing this assessment, you will not only demonstrate your proficiency in data checking but also highlight your commitment to data accuracy and quality. The skills assessed in this evaluation are highly valuable in roles involving data analysis, reporting, and decision-making.

Prepare yourself to carefully scrutinise and validate data, ensuring its accuracy and reliability. Good luck!
Course Overview: This assessment is designed to evaluate your proficiency in verifying and ensuring the accuracy and integrity of data.
Duration (minutes): 90
Units:
- Unit 1: Introduction
  - 1. Data validation: You will be presented with datasets, spreadsheets, or databases containing various types of information. Your task will be to examine the data for inconsistencies, errors, or anomalies, and identify and rectify any inaccuracies.
  - 2. Data completeness: Assessing your ability to ensure that all required fields or data points are present and properly filled. You will need to carefully review the data to identify any missing information and take appropriate actions to address the gaps.
  - 3. Data formatting: You will work with data that requires proper formatting and adherence to specific guidelines or standards. Your task will involve checking for correct data types, formatting rules, and adherence to naming conventions.
  - 4. Cross-referencing and comparisons: Evaluating your capability to cross-check data from multiple sources or datasets to ensure consistency and accuracy. This may involve comparing data across different systems, documents, or periods.
  - 5. Error identification and correction: Testing your ability to identify errors such as duplicate entries, incorrect calculations, or inconsistent data. You will be required to accurately locate these errors and take appropriate measures to correct them.
  - 6. Data integrity: Assessing your understanding of data integrity principles, including maintaining data accuracy, consistency, and reliability. You will be expected to identify and resolve issues that may compromise data integrity, such as data duplication or unauthorised modifications.
  - 7. Attention to detail: Emphasising the importance of being meticulous and thorough in your data-checking process.

Course 271 of 288
Course Name: Implementing and Maintaining Information Systems
Course Description: This course on 'Contribute to the implementation, post-implementation review, and maintenance of information systems' equips participants with the ability to describe and engage in the study, acquisition, implementation, and maintenance of information systems within an accounting environment.
Course Overview: People credited with this unit standard are able to describe and participate in the study, acquisition, implementation and maintenance information systems in an accounting environment.
Duration (minutes): 280
Units:
- Unit 1: Unit 6:  Conduct post-implementation reviews of information systems
  - 1. Appropriate timeframes to follow different types of post-implementation review procedures (e.g., event-driven reviews, time-driven reviews) are determined
  - 2. The factors which must be considered during a post-implementation review (e.g., link between organization's mission and the system, system's performance, implementation costs) are named
  - 3. The actual performance of all system components with their expected performance (e.g., hardware, software, networks, procedures, personnel) are compared
  - 4. The success of the system (e.g., extent to which documented user requirements met) is measured
  - 5. A system's benefits and costs are determined
- Unit 2: Unit 5:  Contribute to the implementation of information systems
  - 1. Project team contribution in system implementation is conducted in a participative manner
  - 2. End-user computing facilities (associated with an information centre) are utilised to implement systems
  - 3. The types of testing and the goal of each type, which should be concluded before a system is installed is described
  - 4. Appropriate test data and test procedures which should be performed successfully before the user accepts a system are identified
  - 5. The steps in installing information systems, and who is responsible for each step (e.g., hardware acquisition, staff training, site preparation) are named
  - 6. The advantages and disadvantages of the types of systems conversion/methods of changeover (e.g., direct conversion, phased conversion, parallel conversion, pilot conversion) are named
- Unit 3: Unit 8:  Establish and evaluate procedure for acquiring information system components
  - 1. The advantages and disadvantages of purchasing, leasing, or renting hardware are named
  - 2. The advantages and disadvantages of building or buying application software are named
  - 3. The steps which should be followed when selecting system components (e.g., document user requirements, document request for proposal, select appropriate software, evaluate possible hardware options) are described
  - 4. The factors which should be considered when selecting application software (e.g., functionality, quality cost, vendor support, hardware platform required) are listed
  - 5. The factors which should be considered when evaluating hardware options (e.g., performance, cost, vendor support) are listed
  - 6. The factors to consider when selecting a vendor (e.g., financial availability, quality of after-sales service, extent of user training offered) are listed
- Unit 4: Unit 3:  Participate in conducting feasibility studies
  - 1. The categories of systems feasibility (e.g., technical, economic, operational, schedule, legal) are named.
  - 2. Cost/benefit analyses of information systems are prepared.
  - 3. Using common techniques to make system selection evaluations (e.g., bench-mark tests, volume sizing, systems sizing) are assisted.
- Unit 5: Unit 7:  Identify types of system maintenance and describe techniques for maintaining and upgrading systems
  - 1. The causes of changes which may need to be made to installed systems (e.g., new user request, technical enhancements, errors in design) are named
  - 2. The types of maintenance, and when each type is appropriate (e.g., patch, release) are identified and described
  - 3. The relationship between maintenance and design (e.g., good design, less expensive maintenance) is defined
  - 4. The financial implication of maintenance (e.g., increase in system's age increases maintenance costs) is determined and described
- Unit 6: Unit 1:  Describe the basic concepts of information systems
  - 1. The concepts of "systems" and "systems thinking" are explained and the types of systems (e.g., stable, simple, open, closed) are named
  - 2. The common characteristics of systems (e.g., subsystems, system boundaries, redundancy, entropy) are named and illustrated
  - 3. The elements of a control/feedback system and the function of each element (e.g., input, process, output, sensor, criteria, activator) are described
  - 4. The nature, types, sources and characteristics of information are compared
  - 5. The relationship between data and information are described
  - 6. The uses, significance and competitive advantage of information are defined
  - 7. The characteristics of each category of the system which can be identified by who in an organisation uses the output from the system (e.g., transaction processing, MIS) are described
  - 8. The characteristics of each category of the system which can be identified by where and when the processing is done (e.g., batch, on-line, centralised, distributed, client-server) are described
  - 9. The phases in the systems development life cycle and the deliverables from each phase are described and the roles and responsibilities of the people involved in developing or maintaining systems.
  - 10. The diagrammatic representation of systems (e.g., data flow, diagrams, hierarchical charts) is explained.
  - 11. An individual's right to privacy and the possible conflicts between these rights and the use of information systems (e.g., unwanted consequences of sharing information (junk mail) are described
- Unit 7: Unit 4:  Specify user information systems requirements
  - 1. The functions of, and information required from a system which is to be implemented are specified.
  - 2. The characteristics required of the system which is to be implemented (e.g., availability, maintainability, usability) are suggested.
  - 3. The appropriate person-machine interfaces of the system are specified.
  - 4. The corporate information required for the company's database which the system must provide is identified.
  - 5. The systems control requirements enabling the system to be audited (e.g., audit trail, levels/types of security) are suggested.
- Unit 8: Unit 2:  Identify basic issues that determine the way computer-based information systems are implemented
  - 1. The opportunities, advantages and risks of using computers in business are discussed.
  - 2. The advantages and disadvantages of purchasing versus developing application software are contrasted
  - 3. The methods, advantages and disadvantages of developing an information system (e.g., end-user computing, in-house development, prototyping, application development tools) are described.
  - 4. The procedures for determining the advantages and disadvantages of using software houses/bureaus to develop information systems (e.g., a request for quotation) are described.
  - 5. The changing role of the user in systems implementation (e.g., from a passive spectator to end-user computing and joint application development sessions) is described.
  - 6. The impact of computer/information technology on society (e.g., ethics, privacy, property rights/intellectual property) is described.
  - 7. The impact of computers/information technology on organisations and the work environments (e.g., change of culture, computer crime, human error and computer malfunction, quality of work life) is described.
  - 8. The impact of computers/information technology on information systems (e.g., increased value of information, risks, controls) is described.
  - 9. The impact of computers/information technology on current legislation (e.g., copyright and privacy laws) is described.

Practical scenarios will be analysed to help you develop professional judgement in line with ethical standards and organisational codes. You will also learn to evaluate and implement ethical procedures, ensuring that your actions and decisions align with both professional and organisational ethical guidelines. By the end of the course, you will be equipped to uphold high ethical standards in your professional practice.
Course Overview: This course teaches you to apply business ethics principles and frameworks in a professional environment to ensure ethical decision-making and behaviour.
Duration (minutes): 170
Units:
- Unit 1: Unit 2: Exercise professional judgement with regard to practical situations
  - 1. Analyse practical situations to enable the practitioner to make professional judgements in relation to the applicable code of professional conduct. 2. Apply professional judgement to practical situations in accordance with the applicable code of professional conduct. Describe the corporate code of ethics of a business/business entity in relation to general principles of corporate behaviour within the organisation and/or profession. 3. Exercise professional judgement in line with the organisational code of ethics.
- Unit 2: Unit 3: Use ethical procedures in a professional environment
  - 1. Ethical procedures are used in the professional environment that comply with the code of professional conduct. 2. Situations are evaluated to judge the professional intervention and procedure that are most appropriate. 3. Procedures are developed and implemented, where necessary, in accordance with organisational and professional ethics.
- Unit 3: Unit 1: Demonstrate an understanding of the concepts and principles relating to business ethics
  - 1. The philosophy and framework of ethical conduct is explained in a meaningful manner. 2. The corporate code of ethics of a corporation/business entity is described in relation to general principles of corporate behaviour within the organisation and/or profession. 3. Codes of professional conduct are explained in accordance with their related regulations.

Course 274 of 288
Course Name: Business Writing Level 4
Course Description: The purpose of the unit standard requires learners to follow a process in writing texts and reports required in business. It is intended to promote clear, unambiguous communication in plain language and to improve the quality of written reports and other texts that are specific to a business environment, require a particular format and may include specified legislated requirements. The unit standard enables learners to recognise and effectively use textual conventions and features specific to business texts.
Course Overview: The purpose of the unit standard requires learners to follow a process in writing texts and reports required in business.
Duration (minutes): 250
Units:
- Unit 1: Unit 3: Compose a text using plain language for a specific function
  - 1. A format and structure are selected for the text that is appropriate for the intended audience and function
  - 2. The main points to be included in the text are identified, and the necessary supporting details are added
  - 3. A first draft of the text is written that collates the necessary information in a rough framework
- Unit 2: Unit 5: Present a written text for a particular function in a business environment
  - 1. A text type, format, and layout are selected that is appropriate for the audience and purpose
  - 2. Layout and formatting techniques are used correctly to enhance the readability of the text
  - 3. Information in the document is evaluated in terms of its appropriateness for the intended audience and business function
  - 4. The final draft is proofread to check that it is completely correct
  - 5. The final copy is self-assessed using a rubric or checklist based on the requirements of the writing task and the items on the checklist created to Identify and collect information needed to write a text specific to a particular function
- Unit 3: Unit 1: Use textual features and conventions specific to business texts for effective writing
  - 1. Texts specific to a particular function in a business environment are identified and an indication is given of industry-specific and/or legislative requirements for each text
  - 2. Texts specific to a particular function in a business environment are produced in response to defined requirements
  - 3. The implications of not following the industry-specific or legislative requirements for a specific type of text are explained and an indication is given of the possible consequences of non-compliance
  - 4.Terminology and conventions specific to a particular function in a business environment are used appropriately
- Unit 4: Unit 4: Organise and structure a text appropriately for a business function
  - 1. The first draft is checked to ensure that appropriate grammar has been used and where necessary the draft is rewritten in plain language using clear accessible language that avoids over-complex syntax.
  - 2. Different ways of presenting the same information are considered and used where these enhance the meaning of the text.
  - 3. Technical or marketing terms and jargon are interpreted and rephrased in plain language or used appropriately in the correct context where the terminology is essential to the understanding of the text.
  - 4. All information is checked for accuracy and factual correctness.
  - 5. The document is ordered to ensure that the sequence is logical and meaningful
- Unit 5: Unit 2: Identify and collect information needed to write a text specific to a particular function
  - 1. The intended or incidental audience for whom the text is to be written are identified for a specific field or subfield to focus the information needs
  - 2. The purpose of the text is identified within a specific field or subfield and according to the information
  - 3. Questions are asked to help understand client needs and to focus on information gathering
  - 4. Information required for the document is accessed from a variety of sources
  - 5. Information accessed is checked for accuracy, bias, stereotypes, and other offensive details
  - 6. The focus of the proposed text is defined, and a decision is made about what information should be included or omitted to ensure the focus
  - 7. A checklist is created to facilitate reflection and editing
- Unit 6: Author
  - SpecCon

Course 277 of 288
Course Name: Conducting Organisational Needs Analysis
Course Description: This course delivers an in-depth exploration of the process of conducting an organisational needs analysis, aligning business objectives with current capabilities to identify key developmental areas. Learners will develop the skills to plan and execute a structured analysis, incorporating valid data collection methods, analytical techniques, and stakeholder engagement strategies. Emphasis is placed on ensuring the relevance, accuracy, and completeness of information, interpreting findings effectively, and documenting processes for validation and decision-making. Key areas of study include defining the purpose and scope of the analysis, verifying organisational objectives with stakeholders, identifying performance gaps, and formulating recommendations for addressing unmet needs. Learners will also develop the ability to prepare professional, well-structured reports that adhere to organisational standards and support strategic planning. By the end of this course, participants will be capable of conducting a robust and systematic needs analysis that supports effective change management, resource allocation, and organisational improvement initiatives.
Course Overview: Strategic insight, organisational alignment, and evidence-based decision-making are at the heart of successful business development. This course provides learners with the essential knowledge and tools to conduct a comprehensive organisational needs analysis. By engaging with stakeholders, evaluating current practices, and identifying strategic gaps, learners will be equipped to provide actionable insights that inform planning, improve performance, and support organisational growth.
Duration (minutes): 180
Units:
- Unit 1: Unit 3: Define the gap and make recommendations for bridging the gap
  - 1. The gap is determined using an acceptable analysis technique appropriate to the context.
  - 2. The gap definition consistently analyses the current situation and objectives. All objectives found to be unaddressed are highlighted and described in terms of a need.
  - 3. The definition of the gap addresses the scope and purpose of the analysis and facilitates further planning and decision-making.
  - 4. Recommendations of methods and scenarios for closing the gap are considered reasonable, effective, and comprehensive.
- Unit 2: Unit 2: Determine and describe the agreed short and long-term organisational objectives
  - 1. The objectives are verified with stakeholders as valid, current, and complete. Key decision-makers are strategists and are included in the verification process.
  - 2. The objectives are recorded clearly to facilitate further interpretation.
  - 3. The role and importance of objectives are described within the context of the analysis, taking cognisance of their function and value to the organisation.
- Unit 3: Unit 1: Analyse the current situation
  - 1. The purpose of the analysis has been established and confirmed with stakeholders.
  - 2. The method and scope of the analysis are planned thoroughly to ensure effective and efficient analysis.
  - 3. The sourced information is current, relevant, and accurate. The information covers the entire planned scope of analysis.
  - 4. The method of analysis used is sufficient and relevant to accurately describe the present situation and meet the purpose of the analysis.
  - 5. Actions, processes, and procedures are recorded to facilitate further interpretation and validation of the analysis.
  - 6. Different methods of analysis and data gathering are described in terms of their strengths, weaknesses, features, and applications.
- Unit 4: Unit 4: Produce a written report of the results
  - 1. The report meets the organisational format specifications. Graphics and tables are used where appropriate to improve the quality and ease of communication.
  - 2. The language medium adheres to organisational language policy. The grammar and syntax conform to international norms.
  - 3. The content accurately reflects the analysis, the objectives, and the recommendations.
  - 4. Support documentation is used when necessary and enhances the potential for understanding the report.
  - 5. Sources are acknowledged according to the organisational format policy.
  - 6. The report is completed within the agreed time frames.
- Unit 5: Author
  - SpecCon Holdings (Pty) Ltd

  - 4. Quantities are measured correctly to within the least step of the instrument
