Course 281 of 288
Course Name: Using Statistics and Probability to Analyse and Communicate Life Problems
Course Description: This course is tailored to meet the Mathematical Literacy requirements of the NQF at Level 4, aiming to empower learners with the ability to confidently and insightfully apply mathematical principles to everyday life. Participants will develop skills in critiquing and utilising data collection techniques, as well as representing data effectively. The course emphasises the use of both theoretical and experimental probability to create models, make predictions, and analyse real-world problems. By the end of the course, learners will be adept at employing statistical and probability models for informed decision-making and problem-solving, thereby becoming self-managing individuals, contributing workers, and active, critically aware citizens in a democratic society.
Course Overview: This course provides an in-depth exploration of statistical methods and probability concepts applied to real-world problems, equipping students with the knowledge and skills to critically interrogate, analyse, and communicate statistical findings in various life contexts. Through structured units and sub-units, learners will be guided through the processes of identifying relevant situations, gathering and organising data, applying appropriate statistical methods, and drawing valid conclusions based on sound reasoning. The course emphasizes both theoretical and practical aspects of data analysis, with a focus on ensuring that findings are accurate, reliable, and clearly communicated to diverse audiences.
Duration (minutes): 210
Units:
- Unit 1: Unit 2: Use theoretical and experimental probability to develop models
  - 1. Experiments and simulations are chosen and/or designed appropriately in terms of the situation to be modelled.
  - 2. Predictions are based on validated experimental or theoretical probabilities.
  - 3. The results of experiments and simulations are interpreted correctly in terms of the real context.
  - 4. The outcomes of experiments and simulations are communicated clearly.
- Unit 2: Unit 1: Critique and use techniques for collecting, organising and representing data
  - 1. Situations or issues that can be dealt with through statistical methods are identified correctly.
  - 2. Appropriate methods for collecting, recording, and organising data are used to maximise efficiency and ensure the resolution of a problem or issue.
  - 3. Data sources and databases are selected in a manner that ensures the representativeness of the sample and the validity of resolutions.
  - 4. Activities that could result in contamination of data are identified, and explanations are provided for the effects of contaminated data.
  - 5. Data is gathered using methods appropriate to the data type and purpose for gathering the data.
  - 6. Data collection methods are used correctly
  - 7. Calculations and the use of statistics are correct
  - 8. Graphical representations and numerical summaries are consistent with the data, clear, and appropriate to the situation and target audience
  - 9. Resolutions for the situation or issue are supported by the data and validated in terms of the context
- Unit 3: Unit 3: Critically interrogate and use probability and statistical models
  - 1. Statistics generated from the data are interpreted meaningfully and interpretations are justified or critiqued.
  - 2. Assumptions made in the collection or generation of data and statistics are defined or critiqued appropriately.
  - 3. Tables, diagrams, charts, and graphs are used or critiqued appropriately in the analysis and representation of data, statistics, and probability values.
  - 4. Predictions, conclusions, and judgments are made on the basis of valid arguments and supporting data, statistics, and probability models.
  - 5. Evaluations of the statistics identify potential sources of bias, errors in measurement, potential uses, and misuses and their effects.

  - 3.Recognising appropriate information resources and organisational procedures for obtaining and distributing confidential information.
  - 4.Liaising with relevant parties and verifying reported information is per requirements, compiling and distributing additional commentary/information where required.

Course 287 of 288
Course Name: Comprehensive Security Risk Training
Course Description: This course examines the key components of maintaining a secure working environment, focusing on proactive strategies that protect both individuals and physical spaces. Learners will explore procedural responses to violent incidents, methods for identifying and reporting suspicious activities, and techniques for securing unauthorised and restricted areas. Through practical scenarios and organisational protocols, the course builds awareness of the responsibilities required to ensure a safe, compliant, and resilient workplace for staff and customers alike.
Course Overview: Beyond locked doors and alarm systems lies the true essence of workplace security—a culture of vigilance, responsibility, and preparedness that safeguards people and assets alike.
Duration (minutes): 90
Units:
- Unit 1: Unit 1: Describe and maintain a secure environment by following the security procedure in accordance with organisational requirements
  - 1. Procedures to maintain a secure working environment are described.
  - 2. A high level of security for staff and customers are explained and maintained, and the impact on the organisation if not doing so is defined.
  - 3. The security procedures to be followed in violent situations are described.
  - 4. The perpetrators within a violent situation are identified, and the correct reporting procedure followed and adhered to under simulated conditions.
  - 5. The correct procedure is followed for reporting suspicious items.
- Unit 2: Unit 2: Secure customer, staff and storage areas from unauthorised access in accordance with organisational requirements
  - 1. The importance of securing unauthorised areas from customer access is explained.
  - 2. Security procedures are described according to organisational requirements.
  - 3. Customer and staff areas are demarcated and secured against unauthorised access.
  - 4. Storage areas are secured against unauthorised access, and reasons for doing so are given.

Course 288 of 288
Course Name: Booking Systems
Course Description: The learner will gain the ability to effectively manage bookings using both manual and computerised systems. This includes determining booking requirements, accurately recording details, and confirming reservations. They will learn to handle booking processes from start to finish, ensuring that all entries are correctly logged and updated in the system. By mastering both traditional and digital methods, learners will be equipped to manage bookings efficiently, provide accurate information, and ensure smooth operation in a variety of administrative settings.
Course Overview: This course covers customer liaison, service promotion, booking confirmations, amendments, and system troubleshooting. Learners will gain skills to handle records, coordinate with departments, and ensure smooth service delivery, enhancing customer satisfaction and business success.
Duration (minutes): 170
Units:
- Unit 1: Unit 7: Explain the importance of keeping other departments informed of current and future bookings
  - 1. Departments who should be informed of bookings in the organisation are identified and reasons for informing these in terms of service delivery are provided.
  - 2. The potential impacts on customer service in the event of other departments not being informed of bookings are explained by means of examples.
- Unit 2: Unit 6: Explain the reasons for keeping bookings up to date and following up on unconfirmed bookings
  - 1. Different organisational booking records are identified in terms of their use in relation to organisational administration.
  - 2. Processes and procedures for unconfirmed bookings follow up are described in line with organisational requirements.
- Unit 3: Unit 19: Describe how performance would be adapted in a different type of establishment
  - 1. Identify a range of different establishment types within the hospitality industry and explain how performance to maintain a booking system will be adapted in these organisational types.
- Unit 4: Unit 18: Describe a situation where a guest's booking was incorrectly cancelled
  - 1. Interventions to solve incorrect cancellations of guest bookings are identified and explained in relation to booking system requirements and customer service.
  - 2. Incorrect cancellations are rectified in line with client needs and available services and facilities.
- Unit 5: Unit 17: Carry out all work in an organised and efficient manner taking account of priorities
  - 1. Methods of prioritisation are identified and applied to their own area of responsibility.
  - 2. Work-related to own area of responsibility are planned and executed in order to meet operational requirements.
- Unit 6: Unit 16: Given a system failure or error in manual systems, decide what action to take
  - 1. Possible system failures or errors are identified and relevant action to address problems are explained by means of an example.
- Unit 7: Unit 13: Provide customers with confirmations of bookings and all relevant information
  - 1. Relevant details pertaining to booking confirmations are identified in order to prepare customer confirmations.
  - 2. Booking confirmations are prepared in line with organisational and system requirements.
- Unit 8: Unit 5: Explain the importance of taking deposits in terms of "no shows"
  - 1. The purpose of deposits is explained in relation to service delivery in the hospitality industry as well as business risk and impact in the event of no-shows.
- Unit 9: Unit 11: Offer alternative facilities to customers and explain the importance of doing this
  - 1. The reasons for offering alternative facilities to customers in the event of service and facility unavailability are explained in terms of its impact on customer service, business and impact on the financial bottom line.
  - 2. Alternative services and facilities are identified and offered to customers in line with identified client needs.
- Unit 10: Unit 15: Given a range of amendments, choose a procedure and give reasons for the method chosen
  - 1. Types of possible amendments to bookings are identified in relation to booking requirements and administration.
  - 2. Procedures for amendments are identified and executed for a range of booking amendment types so as to meet standard operational requirements.
  - 3. Booking amendments are communicated with customers in line with organisational requirements.
- Unit 11: Unit 12: Given a range of bookings, take down the details and record the booking
  - 1. Booking details to be recorded are identified and listed in line with booking system and organisational requirements.
  - 2. Different types of bookings are transacted in order to meet booking and administrative requirements.
- Unit 12: Unit 8: Given a range of customers, deal with customers politely and efficiently
  - 1. Different internal and external customers to the organisation are identified and described.
  - 2. Interaction with customers is conducted in line with organisational customer liaison and service requirements.
- Unit 13: Unit 2: Explain the importance of giving accurate information to customers and the need to be aware of time
  - 1. Establishment information relevant to booking requirements is determined in relation to services and facilities offered by the organisation.
  - 2. The maintaining of a sense of urgency in relating service and facilities information to guests in support of bookings are explained with specific reference to customer service and impact on the financial bottom line.
- Unit 14: Unit 1: Demonstrate maintaining a booking service
  - 1. Liaison with a range of customers is demonstrated so as to meet booking and industry requirements.
  - 2. The provision of accurate information in order to meet enquiry needs is demonstrated in accordance with organisational requirements.
  - 3. The promoting of an establishment's services and facilities is demonstrated according to organisational requirements.
  - 4. Service availability and facilities checking are demonstrated according to operational standards and requirements.
  - 5. The offering of alternative facilities to customers are demonstrated according to operational requirements.
  - 6. The recording of a booking is demonstrated so as to meet operational requirements, using a manual or computerised booking system; given a range of bookings.
  - 7. The providing of booking confirmations and all relevant information is demonstrated so as to comply with organisational requirements.
  - 8. The confirming of bookings and deposits from customers is demonstrated as appropriate to organisational requirements.
  - 9. The handling of a real or simulated system failure or error in manual systems are demonstrated so as to meet organisational requirements.
  - 10. The carrying out of all work in an organised and efficient manner is demonstrated, taking account of priorities and complying with organisational requirements.
- Unit 15: Unit 14: Confirm the bookings and request deposits from customers
  - 1. Prepared booking confirmations are forwarded to customers in line with organisational requirements.
  - 2. Deposit requirements are calculated and requested in line with standard operational procedures.
- Unit 16: Unit 3: Explain the reasons for providing an efficient service in terms of company profitability and repeat guest business
  - 1. Reasons for providing efficient service to customers are explained in terms of company profitability and obtaining of repeat business from the guest.
- Unit 17: Unit 9: Promote the establishment's services and facilities at all appropriate times and explain why
  - 1. Reasons for the promotion of the services and facilities are explained in relation to customer needs, service and the impact on the financial bottom line.
  - 2. Different services and facilities are promoted in support of service delivery within the organisation.
- Unit 18: Unit 4: Explain the need to meet customer expectations in terms of knowledge of services and facilities
  - 1. Service and facilities of the organisation are identified and described in relation to customer needs.
  - 2. The importance of service and facilities knowledge is described with specific reference to bookings, calculation of deposits and the impact on the financial bottom line.
- Unit 19: Unit 10: Determine the availability of services and facilities correctly and communicate this clearly to the guest
  - 1. The methods used to determine the availability of services and facilities are explained in line with organisational processes and procedures.
  - 2. The availability of a range of services and facilities are checked in relation to booking enquiries and client needs.
- Unit 20: Author: Hein van Der Westhuizen
  - Heinrich van der Westhuizen is a chartered accountant (CA) by profession, bringing a wealth of financial expertise from his years in the corporate world. However, his entrepreneurial spirit and keen eye for opportunity led him to recognize a significant gap in the market for computer training. In response to this need, he founded SpecCon in 2013, a venture dedicated to providing top-notch computer skills training.
  - As the driving force behind SpecCon, Heinrich has established himself as one of the foremost authorities in Excel skills and beyond. His dedication to excellence and his commitment to delivering high-quality training have propelled SpecCon to prominence in the industry over the past decade. Under his leadership, the company has experienced remarkable growth, fueled by Heinrich's vision and passion for empowering individuals with essential digital skills.
  - Beyond his professional pursuits, Heinrich is a devoted family man and an avid golfer. His love for golf provides a balance to his busy entrepreneurial life, while his commitment to his family underscores his values of connection and support. With his expertise in finance, his entrepreneurial acumen, and his passion for empowering others, Heinrich van der Westhuizen continues to make a lasting impact in both the business world and the community at large.

Course 289 of 289
Course Name: The Composition of a Selected New Ventures Industry/Sector and Its Procurement Systems
Course Description: This course provides a comprehensive exploration of the composition of a selected new ventures industry or sector and its procurement systems. Learners will study value chains, supply chain structures, and communication channels, applying these insights to real business contexts. Attention is given to preparing effective sales pitches, understanding the role of industries in the national economy, and exploring methods of obtaining and sustaining business. The course further examines funding options, role-players in business success, joint ventures, procurement practices, and documentation. Learners will also gain practical skills in recording, controlling, and managing materials within a business context. By the end, participants will have a thorough understanding of how ventures operate within their industry and how procurement systems support sustainable growth.
Course Overview: The success of any new venture depends on understanding its industry landscape, supply chains, and procurement systems. This course equips learners with the knowledge to analyse value chains, navigate supply and communication networks, and apply procurement practices effectively. By mastering these areas, learners will be able to position their venture competitively, secure funding, and deliver on projects with efficiency and professionalism.
Duration (minutes): 200
Units:
- Unit 1: Unit 3: Demonstrate an understanding of different procurement systems that may apply in specific sector/industry
  - 1. Methods for identifying procurement and logistical needs are described with examples.  
2. An understanding of typical procurement documents that apply to industry is demonstrated and completed with examples (typical procurement documents include but are not limited to order forms, quotations, letters and contracts).
3. Typical methods of recording and controlling delivery and usage of materials are described according to own business context (typical procurement control methods include but are not limited to expediting, receiving, returns, stock control, stock control systems).
- Unit 2: Unit 2: Identify the business principles and processes within a selected sector or industry environment
  - 1. Methods of obtaining business are identified for own business context. 
2. The areas of venture funding are understood and explained with examples.
3. All role-players in the success of the selected venture are identified in order to ensure that sales and negotiations are planned effectively.
4. Where necessary, joint ventures or sub-contractor relations are established to deliver on larger projects.
- Unit 3: Unit 1: Identify and analyse the value chain within a selected industry or sector
  - 1. Value chains are understood and explained within the context of own sector/industry.
2. The chains of command within the supply chain are identified and explained in relation to own business:  Chains of command include but are not limited to the range of influence that the various role-players have on new venture in respect of product/service delivery and the ability to sell the product/service to decision-makers, including the chain of command of the client, project manager, specialist etc. 
3. Sales pitches to clients are prepared and positioned according to the identified chains of command.
4. Communication channels within industry/sector role-players are identified, explained and utilised appropriately to ensure effective sales results.
5. The role of the chosen industry/sector in the National Economy and the effect of productivity on that role is identified so that sales pitches are effective.
